<p>Education: is proved to have significant effect on women's health and reproductive behavior through its influence on age at marriage, contraception and health care use, and awareness of risks and danger signs.</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Women's reproductive and health behavior: Reproductive and health behavior involves, for example, the age at which a woman becomes pregnant, whether the pregnancy is wanted, and what kind of health care the woman seeks.</li>
<li>Access to and control of income and resources: Women's income, access to household resources, and power to make decisions influence their ability to seek and utilize health services.</li>
<li>Political commitment: Political commitment is crucial to allocate the available resources and to provide services which are accessible to those most in need.</li>
<li>Low social status of women: The health and well-being of women is related and highly influenced with their social status. Low social status leads to severe burden &amp; over work (Conjugal, maternal, domestic, and professional) exposing to physically demanding activities.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="haemorrhage">Haemorrhage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#haemorrhage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It can occur during pregnancy, delivery or postpartum period. (Antepartum, intrapartum and postpartum)</p>
<p>Trauma/ tears, Tissues, Tone</p>
<p>During pregnancy it can occur at the;</p>
<ul>
<li>1st trimester due to abortion</li>
<li>2nd trimester due to placental location and pre term labour</li>
<li>3rd trimester due to abnormal placental location, premature separation of placenta, and premature labour</li>
</ul>
<p>During delivery due to;</p>
<ul>
<li>Uterine or placental bleeding</li>
<li>Traumatic damage to Vagina or cervix</li>
</ul>
<p>During postpartum period due to:
Non-involution of the uterus
Haemorrhage is more common among multiparous women</p>
<ul>
<li>Unsafe abortion</li>
<li>Prolonged labour</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>Retained placenta and it is also common among women with a history of problems in delivering the placenta.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-cause-for-antepartum-haemorrhage">Predisposing cause for Antepartum haemorrhage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-cause-for-antepartum-haemorrhage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Placenta praevia</li>
<li>Placenta abruption
Predisposing cause for abruptio placenta;</li>
<li>Common in patients with hypertension</li>
<li>Trauma</li>
<li>Injuries to abdomen</li>
<li>Excessively hard work</li>
<li>Emotional trauma</li>
<li>Common in multiparity</li>
<li>Increases with age</li>
<li>Scarred uterus</li>
<li>Multiple pregnancy</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-cause-for-post-partum-haemorrhage">Predisposing cause for Post partum haemorrhage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-cause-for-post-partum-haemorrhage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Atonic uterus</li>
<li>History of postpartum haemorrhage, increased chance for recurrence</li>
<li>High parity</li>
<li>Multiple pregnancy</li>
<li>Anemia – causing poor contraction</li>
<li>Prolonged labour</li>
<li>Trauma – this can show quality of care</li>
</ul>
<p>Most primary postpartum haemorrhage results either from failure of the uterus to contract and remain contracted or from retained placenta (partial or complete). WHO has recommended that midwives be trained to perform manual removal of the placenta, because the results in terms of blood loss, infection and mortality are best when this is done within an hour of delivery.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="infection">Infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Infection is prevalent among the disadvantaged and risk increases by factors like anemia, malaria, goiter, and malnutrition. Maternal infection is a serious problem as a result of the vicious cycle caused by low caloric intake, heavy workload and infection.</p>
<p>It is also compounded by pregnancies at young age and too many pregnancies too close together.</p>

<p>Poverty also perpetuates the problem through illiteracy, poor sanitation, inadequate housing (crowding), and Inadequate and unsafe water.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-puerperal-sepsis">a. Puerperal Sepsis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-puerperal-sepsis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Puerperal sepsis occurs following long and complicated deliveries and it is rare in uncomplicated spontaneous delivery.</p>
<p>Sepsis is also very common after unsafe abortion.</p>
<p>Usually, sepsis is fatal when the mother's condition is compromised due to difficult labour and severe bleeding.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="important-factors-that-are-related-with-and-increase-the-risk-are">Important factors that are related with and increase the risk are:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#important-factors-that-are-related-with-and-increase-the-risk-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Majority deliver at home and expose to poor sterile procedure</li>
<li>Assistance by Untrained person during delivery</li>
<li>Vaginal examination with unclean hands during delivery and number of vaginal examinations</li>
<li>Prolonged labour (the larger it lasts the greater the risk)</li>
<li>Duration of ruptured membrane before delivery (increase chance of the liquor to become infected)</li>
<li>Use of Instruments to assist delivery</li>
<li>Trauma</li>
<li>Caesarean section specially in ruptured uterus</li>
<li>Pre-existing genital and reproductive tract infections</li>
<li>Those who survive infection face increased risk of</li>
<li>Pelvic inflammatory disease</li>
<li>Infertility, and Ectopic pregnancy</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effective-strategies-to-prevent-sepsis-include">Effective strategies to prevent sepsis include:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effective-strategies-to-prevent-sepsis-include" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Improvement in standards of hygiene in routine care.</li>
<li>Keeping interventions and vaginal examinations to a minimum</li>
<li>Provision of “clean delivery” for all women. Basic aseptic technique is simple in facilities with adequate supplies of water, soap and disinfectant.</li>
</ul>
<p>One of the primary aims of trained birth attendant training programs throughout the developing world is to promote clean delivery in the home through deduction and provision of basic supplies such as:</p>
<p>sterile razor blades and washable plastic sheets.</p>
<p>It is, however, difficult to ensure cleanliness in all deliveries, particularly where access to clean water is limited.</p>
<ul>
<li>Referring women with pre-term prolonged rupture of membranes (longer than 12 hours) to a referral-level facility for assessment.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Use of prophylactic antibiotics following pre-labour rupture of membranes (longer than 12 hours).</li>
<li>Transferring women with prolonged labour (longer than 12 hours) to a referral-level facility.</li>
<li>Evacuating retained placental fragments promptly.</li>
</ul>
<p>Early detection and timely use of antibiotics for postpartum sepsis reduces the risk of mortality or long-term sequelae.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="malaria">Malaria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#malaria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Malaria is cause of severe underweight during birth and 3 million infants are affected in Africa. It is common at first pregnancy.</p>
<p>During pregnancy the risk of getting malaria increases two times and the risk for cerebral malaria is high. During pregnancy malaria is also the cause of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Severe anemia</li>
<li>Spontaneous abortion</li>
<li>Pre mature labour</li>
<li>Still birth, and</li>
<li>Low birth weight</li>
</ul>
<p>Wherever malaria is common pregnant women should take anti-malarial tablets throughout pregnancy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="anaemic-women-due-to-malaria-face">Anaemic women due to malaria face<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anaemic-women-due-to-malaria-face" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Risk during child bearing</li>
<li>Less tolerance to blood loss (bleeding)</li>
<li>Risk for anaesthesia and operative delivery</li>
<li>Poor pregnancy outcome</li>
<li>Bleeding, illness, and death during delivery</li>
<li>Still birth</li>
<li>Poor foetal growth</li>
<li>Pre term labour</li>
<li>Low birth weight (serious effect on infancy)</li>
</ul>
<p>When anaemia is severe pregnant mothers face (directly) congestive heart failure and haemorrhage (indirectly). This can happen in 3-9% of pregnant mothers. In moderate cases of anaemia there will be poor ability to recover form haemorrhage and infection</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hepatitis">Hepatitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hepatitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<p>Hepatitis A is related with socio economic status and usually women of low socio economic status (SES) are susceptible as a result of poor hygienic conditions.</p>
<p>Faecal contamination of food &amp; water are responsible as the mode of transmission.</p>
<p>Incidence during pregnancy increases two times and pregnant are more seriously ill and likely to die than non-pregnant women. In Ethiopia it is reported as one of the major causes of maternal death due to infectious diseases. Premature labour, liver failure, and severe haemorrhage are common complications of severe hepatitis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sexually-transmitted-diseases-and-pelvic-infections">Sexually Transmitted Diseases and Pelvic Infections:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexually-transmitted-diseases-and-pelvic-infections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sexually transmitted diseases and pelvic infections have grave consequence on mother and child. They can result from</p>
<ul>
<li>Sexual activity</li>
<li>Poor obstetric and gynecological practices specially associated with Induced abortion, spontaneous abortion and childbirth</li>
</ul>
<p>Fatality depends on the type of organism and the organs affected.</p>
<p>Its effects and complications include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Tubal scarring leading to infertility</li>
<li>Ectopic pregnancy</li>
<li>Spontaneous abortion</li>
<li>Pre mature rupture of membrane</li>
<li>Congenital anomalies such as blindness, and mental retardation etc.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="acquired-immuno-deficiency-syndrome-aids">Acquired Immuno Deficiency Syndrome (AIDS)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acquired-immuno-deficiency-syndrome-aids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The spread of AIDS is increasing and rapid specially in sub-Saharan Africa and other developing countries putting stress on the already strained health care system.</p>
<p>Magnitude:</p>
<p>According to the WHO estimate 16,000 people are infected every day and there are 3 million infected women and it is becoming a serious threat and alarmingly increasing in pregnancy. In countries like Rwanda 18.30% of women who came for Ante Natal Care were found to be HIV positive in a routine screening.</p>
<p>This condition is further aggravated as a woman with AIDS has a 25-40% chance of passing on HIV in the womb or at birth (the number of children born with HIV is reported to be 3.8 million).</p>
<p>AIDS is expected to be the major cause of maternal mortality.</p>
<p>Poverty is also related with AIDS and as a cause of death. Some of the reasons are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Poor health care</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Poor availability of drugs for protection of immunity and increasing survival Immunity</li>
<li>Crowding (increases transmission)</li>
<li>Malnutrition further lowers immunity for common diseases like water borne infections etc.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-2-antenatal-care">2.2 Antenatal Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-2-antenatal-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ante Natal Care (ANC) is the care given to pregnant mothers that they have safe pregnancy and healthy baby.</p>
<p>It also helps in minimizing complications of pregnancy, labour the post partum and neonatal periods.</p>
<p>The purpose of ANC is to care for pregnant mothers and to have all births attended by trained health workers, and to identify pregnancies where risk is high and provide special care for the mother and the infant.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="activities-during-the-first-ante-natal-care-visit">Activities During the First Ante Natal Care Visit<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#activities-during-the-first-ante-natal-care-visit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Diagnose pregnancy</li>
<li>History taking</li>
<li>Physical Examination</li>
<li>Laboratory Examination. Haemoglobin measurement. VDRL test for syphilis is one of the important tests to be done irrespective of any condition provided that the facilities are available. Because syphilis has a grave impact on the foetus then on the new born.</li>
<li>Immunisation: give Tetanus Toxoid injection. If first time repeat after one month.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Protection</strong>: 2 doses of tetanus toxoid protect for 3 years, 3 doses for 5 years, 4 doses for 10 years and 5 doses for life.</p>
<ul>
<li>Detect and treat anaemia</li>
<li>Detect and treat syphilis and other problems accordingly</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="second-and-following-anc-visits">Second and Following ANC Visits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#second-and-following-anc-visits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Measure blood pressure</li>
<li>Measure the symphasis fundal height</li>
<li>Tetanus Toxoid and other examinations as indicated</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="health-and-nutrition-education-during-anc">Health and Nutrition Education During ANC<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-and-nutrition-education-during-anc" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It must focus on:</p>
<ul>
<li>Pregnancy: foetal movement (specially for primigravida), labour and common problems</li>
<li>Diet and Nutrition: extra food, weight gains, fasting and rest</li>
<li>Avoiding alcohol, tobacco, and drugs (specially in the first trimester)</li>
<li>Personal hygiene</li>
</ul>

<ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="weight-gain-during-pregnancy">Weight Gain During Pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#weight-gain-during-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pre-pregnancy weight and weight gain in pregnancy are both critical and additive in their effect on pregnancy outcome. Equal emphasis should be given to assuring that both are normal.</p>
<p>A pregnant mother has to have weight measurement a month apart, anytime during the second or third trimester. A gain of less than one kg per month is the danger signal, with no weight gain or weight loss being even more severe and calling for immediate action, such as food supplementation directly for the woman.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risk-factors-identifiable-in-anc-include">Risk factors identifiable in ANC include:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors-identifiable-in-anc-include" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Age under 18 or above 35</li>
<li>Primigravida</li>
<li>Previous caesarean section, vacuum, or forceps delivery</li>
<li>Previous perinatal death, stillbirth</li>
<li>Previous Post partum haemorrhage</li>
<li>Previous ante partum haemorrhage</li>
<li>More than 6 pregnancies</li>
<li>Twins</li>
<li>Hydramnios</li>
<li>Pre-eclampsia</li>
<li>Diabetes, cardiac problem, renal disease etc.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="infections-during-pregnancy">Infections During Pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#infections-during-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pregnant women are sexually active and at risk of sexually transmitted disease, including HIV/AIDS. In prenatal care screening and treatment for syphilis is routine and is a cost-effective intervention.</p>
<p>Many studies in developing countries have demonstrated high prevalence levels of both syphilis and gonorrhea in pregnant women, leading to considerable long-term morbidity in women, and to congenital disease and prenatal mortality.</p>
<p>Researchers estimate that of those women, who are currently pregnant, 10 to 15 percent have syphilis and two-thirds of all these pregnancies have an adverse outcome.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Reliable screening tests exist for both syphilis and gonorrhoea, as do safe, effective treatments. Screening can be conducted in the clinic while women are attending and treatment started immediately.</p>
<p>Women are at higher risk of AIDS because the two predominant modes of transmission of HIV infection are sexual and prenatal.</p>
<p>In the case of HIV, curative treatment is not available, and even treatment to delay the onset of symptomatic disease with antiviral drugs is not readily available or affordable in developing countries. However, some of the most effective strategies for sexually transmitted diseases are equally important for AIDS prevention.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="strategies-in-preventing-transmission-include">Strategies in preventing transmission include :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#strategies-in-preventing-transmission-include" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Promoting education strategies that modify or eliminate risk behaviours</li>
<li>Providing adequate diagnostic and treatment facilities for patients</li>
<li>Limiting complications by early detection and adequate treatment;</li>
<li>Reducing the risk of infection during genital tract procedures through safe delivery procedures</li>
<li>Reducing exposure to infection by offering health education;</li>
<li>Limiting further transmission through counselling and partner referral and</li>
<li>Promoting condom use and targeting family planning programs more aggressively toward men.</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment of <strong>symptomatic urinary tract infections</strong> is important, and it has been shown that screening for asymptomatic bacteriuria, followed by appropriate antibiotic treatment, <strong>reduces the incidence of pyelonephritis in the mother, as well as the incidence of low weight and premature delivery</strong>.</p>
<p>The increased risk of low-birth-weight babies and the risk of neonatal and infant mortality associated with low birth weight are of major concern in areas of endemic malaria.</p>
<p>Chorio-amnionitis and fetal infection and loss can be prevented through prompt referral of women with pre-term or pre-labour rupture of the membranes and prophylactic use of antibiotics.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="role-of-trained-traditional-birth-attendants-ttba-s">Role of Trained Traditional Birth Attendants (TTBA's)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-of-trained-traditional-birth-attendants-ttba-s" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In general Trained traditional birth attendants are important and helpful in advising and referring during pregnancy &amp; delivery. Because TTBA's can easily identify problems such as</p>
<ul>
<li>Young primigravida</li>
<li>Previous pregnancy problems</li>
<li>Short stature (depending on local norms of risk)</li>
</ul>

<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Bleeding before or during labour</li>
<li>Pre mature rupture of membrane</li>
</ul>
<p>TBAS - assist 60% -80% deliveries throughout the world are called by different names such as “comadrone” co mother of clients in Latin America. The name explains their importance. One of the primary <strong>aims of trained birth attendant training programs throughout the developing world is to promote clean delivery</strong> in the home through deduction and provision of basic supplies such as:</p>
<p>sterile razor blades and washable plastic sheets. It is, however, difficult to ensure cleanliness in all deliveries, particularly where access to clean water is limited.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assignment-on-danger-sings-of-pregnancy-by-alvin">ASSIGNMENT ON DANGER SINGS OF PREGNANCY... <div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-3-infant-health">2.3: Infant Health:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-3-infant-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An infant: this a child under the age of one year (0-12 months)</p>
<p>A newborn is from age 0-28 days</p>
<p>Newborn health is primarily categorized into 2</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-immediate-newborn-care">1 Immediate newborn care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-immediate-newborn-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-daily-routine-newborn-care">2 Daily routine newborn care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-daily-routine-newborn-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<p>It includes;</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="screening">Screening<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#screening" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>One of the most neglected services which is often forgotten is screening.</p>
<p>It is a very important activity which has to be carried out every day in all institutions delivering child health services.</p>
<p>There is an immense benefit for children, as well as to their mothers, by the brief assessment (history and physical examination) at every visit to the clinic.</p>
<p>Screening is an important tool to avoid "missed opportunities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="expanded-program-on-immunization-epi">Expanded Program on Immunization (EPI)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#expanded-program-on-immunization-epi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Immunisation is the process of protecting a person from a specific disease.</p>
<p>It is protection of a susceptible host from a specific disease by administration of</p>
<ul>
<li>A living modified agent</li>
<li>A suspension of killed organism</li>
<li>An attenuated toxin.</li>
</ul>
<p>Immunisation decreases susceptibility by producing antibodies or sensitised cells to fight the agent and its product.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-immunisations">Types of Immunisations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-immunisations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Active - Vaccine which acts in place of natural antigen</li>
<li>Passive - ready-made antibodies and our body do not take in the making. E.g. Foetus, TAT, snake antiserum.</li>
</ul>
<p>Another classification can be:</p>
<ul>
<li>Natural such as Mother to foetus, infection</li>
<li>Artificially induced immunisation such as vaccine (antigen), antibodies</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="herd-immunity">Herd Immunity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#herd-immunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Herd immunity indicate that large proportion of people in a certain community are immune. The implication is when there are few susceptible, the natural infection cannot keep going in the community and incidence goes down to a low level.</p>
<p>For immunisation to be effective in controlling communicable disease; 75% of the population and 75% of new-borns have to be vaccinated.</p>
<p>Discontinuing vaccination programs have serious risk of causing an epidemic.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="objectives-of-epi">Objectives of EPI<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives-of-epi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>To reduce morbidity and mortality from six major diseases - diphtheria, pertussis, tetanus, measles, poliomyelitis and tuberculosis by immunising all children throughout the world by 1990.</li>
<li>To promote national self-reliance in delivering immunization services within comprehensive health services.</li>
<li>To promote regional self-reliance in vaccine production and quality control.</li>
</ol>
<p>The activities outlined were:</p>
<ul>
<li>Provide immunization or information about immunization at every health contact</li>
<li>Reduce dropout rates between the first and last immunization's</li>
<li>Increase the priority given to control of measles, polio and neonatal tetanus</li>
<li>Improve immunization services to the poor in urban areas</li>
<li>Use special approaches such as national immunization days, where they strengthen the health infrastructure and contribute to a sustained improvement in coverage.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="strategies-to-conduct-epi-sessions">Strategies to conduct EPI sessions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#strategies-to-conduct-epi-sessions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Fixed (static) facilities offering immunization every day in all health institutions.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages">Advantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>No additional costs for transportation</li>
<li>Personnel who can give injections and instructing parents are already available as is basic medical equipment</li>
<li>Easier to keep vaccines at proper temperatures</li>
</ul>
<p>54</p>
<ul>
<li>Client records may more easily established and kept up to date</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages">Disadvantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Parents must travel long distance to bring children to health centers. The further parents travel, the less likely they are to come for immunizations.</li>
<li>Absence of integrated health service</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-outreach-services-and-mobile-teams">2. Outreach services and mobile teams<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-outreach-services-and-mobile-teams" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Important, especially for children in remote rural areas and poor urban as well as other children whose parents are unable or unwilling to come to health institutions</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="disadvantage">Disadvantage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Scheduling visits and adhering to schedules are difficult because of transportation</li>
<li>Problems or poor weather.</li>
<li>Outreach services and mobile teams can be expensive.</li>
<li>Staff need to be paid per diem</li>
<li>Vehicles much be bought and maintained.</li>
<li>Strict reminding is necessary for parents to be available on the days of appointment</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-intensive-immunization-campaigns">3. Intensive immunization campaigns<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-intensive-immunization-campaigns" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This consists of regularly repeated mass campaigns which are mounted to stop epidemic by quickly immunising as many susceptible people as possible.</p>
<p>These campaigns have sharply increased vaccine coverage, especially, those of single dose vaccines.</p>
<p>Such campaigns can involve non health workers for polio vaccination as it is given orally.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="antigens">Antigens<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antigens" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Antigens given are: Bacterium Culmette Guirrin (BCG, for tuberculosis), DPT (diphtheria, pertussis, tetanus), OPV (oral polio vaccine), Measles vaccine, tetanus toxoid for reproductive age and pregnant women.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="types-of-vaccine-for-epi">Types of Vaccine for EPI<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-vaccine-for-epi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Vaccines can be killed microorganisms, live but weakened (attenuated) or toxoid, i.e., harmless forms of toxins or poisons that the bacteria produce.</p>
<ul>
<li>Killed vaccines are DPT and TT, which should be kept just above freezing point in the refrigerator (0 - 8C).</li>
<li>Live attenuated vaccines are measles, polio and BCG. These should be deeply frozen, at around -20C. Since BCG is sensitive to UV light and heat, it is packaged in coloured vials and they should be protected against the sunlight.</li>
</ul>

<p>2.4: Birth Planning:</p>
<p>A birth plan is an outline of your preferences during your labor and delivery. For example, your birth plan may include who you want with you during labor, whether you want pain meds, or if you want the lights dimmed. You can include anything you think will make your labor and birth more comfortable for you.</p>
<p>What's valuable about birth plans is that they give the expectant mother a 'voice' for her body and a say in the decisions that are made. Birth plans can also be useful in supporting people so they feel included in the baby's birth and they play an advocacy role for the woman if she cannot communicate clearly for herself.</p>
<p>Developing your birth plan</p>
<p>Every woman's birth plan will be different because what goes in it depends on what's important to you. A well-presented and easy-to-follow birth plan will allow your carers to see at a glance what is important to you and what your preferences are. A birth plan should be discussed well in advance of giving birth.</p>
<p>Birth plan template</p>
<p>Following is a list of suggested headings you might consider using in your birth plan, with an explanation under each. You certainly do not have to use all of them. Maybe only a few are really important to you. You might want to include other aspects of your care that are not listed here. Some content will include; Birth location, the birthing environment, fetal well being and assessment, support person and companion, labour preference measures (i.e. nutrition, blood products, birthing positions, water births etc), pan relief, birth attendants, labour management, delivery</p>
<ul>
<li>Birth companions</li>
</ul>
<p>List the people you want to be with you during labour. This might include your partner, parents or sisters. You might have employed a private midwife or doula, or you might want your general practitioner (GP) there if you have used one under a 'shared care' arrangement during your pregnancy.</p>
<ul>
<li>Environment</li>
</ul>
<p>List any specific preferences you have for your birthing environment, such as particular music playing, aromatherapy or dimmed lighting (candles or naked flames are not allowed).</p>
<p>Most hospitals can accommodate these kinds of requests but it is worth checking first, particularly if something is very important to you.</p>
<ul>
<li>Labour pain relief</li>
</ul>
<p>Note down the kinds of pain relief you want to use, which may include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>massage</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>TENS machine</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>gas</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>pethidine</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>epidural.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Positions for labour and birth</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>List any preferences you have for birthing positions. These might include lying on the bed, kneeling, standing or squatting. Mention if you would like to use particular equipment such as a birthing stool, Swiss ball, mat or beanbag.</p>
<ul>
<li>Assisted delivery</li>
</ul>
<p>You might want to note down a preference for forceps or ventouse (where a suction cup is attached to the baby's head by a vacuum being created in the cup) if you need some help to deliver your baby.</p>
<ul>
<li>Delivery of the placenta</li>
</ul>
<p>In your third stage of labour, delivery of the placenta, you may have an injection to reduce the risk of maternal bleeding or postpartum haemorrhage. Write down if you want this to happen or if you would prefer a less managed approach.</p>
<ul>
<li>Your baby's umbilical cord</li>
</ul>
<p>Write down if you would like someone in particular (such as your partner) to cut the umbilical cord. You could also mention if you would prefer delayed cord clamping. This is where the umbilical cord is not clamped or cut until after pulsations have stopped or until after the placenta is delivered.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>57</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Delayed cord clamping is an increasingly popular practice (many services now do this routinely) because delaying the clamping of the cord can mean your newborn ends up with more blood volume than it would have if the cord had been clamped immediately.</p>
<p>If your baby requires emergency treatment delayed cord clamping will not be an option.</p>
<ul>
<li>Procedures you would like to avoid</li>
</ul>
<p>If there are particular procedures you would like to avoid, if possible, it is important to list them. These could include induction, artificial rupture of the membranes or the use of forceps. Although your preference may be not to have certain procedures, sometimes they are medically indicated for the wellbeing of your baby.</p>
<ul>
<li>Postnatal care</li>
</ul>
<p>Check your maternity hospital or birthing centre's policy for how your baby will be cared for immediately after birth. Will the baby be checked and tested first or will you have the opportunity to bond with skin-to-skin contact straight away while the midwife undertakes tests? If you have a preference, write it down in your birth plan.</p>
<ul>
<li>Feeding your baby</li>
</ul>
<p>Be clear in your birth plan about whether you prefer to breastfeed or formula feed your baby. If you do not want your baby to have bottles or formula, say so.</p>
<ul>
<li>Special needs</li>
</ul>
<p>If you have additional needs, such as mobility or religious or cultural needs, note these down in your birth plan, specifying any support you require.</p>
<p>If you have a disability, write about the kind of help you will need during labour and after the birth. Mention any special equipment that would help you.</p>
<p>If you require a special diet during your hospital stay or would like certain rituals carried out when your baby is born, have these detailed in your plan.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sharing-your-birth-plan">Sharing your birth plan<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sharing-your-birth-plan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ideally, it is best to share your birth plan with your caregivers and ask them to go through it with you during one of your pregnancy appointments. This will give you a chance to ask</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>questions and decide together whether your preferences are suitable given your health and medical history.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="when-things-do-not-go-to-plan">When things do not go to plan<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#when-things-do-not-go-to-plan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The most important thing to remember about a birth plan is that births do not always go to plan! Unexpected complications may arise or you might change your mind once you are in the delivery room. Some women are adamant about refusing all labour pain-relieving drugs but change their mind once they experience the pain. It is okay to change your mind.</p>
<p>You might have your heart set on a home birth but your medical history might mean it is simply too dangerous. Medical issues that arise during your labour might mean you need to have a caesarean section or that your vaginal birth needs some assistance - such as forceps.</p>
<p>Be open to last-minute changes. Your health and the health of your baby are the most important things.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="where-to-get-help">Where to get help<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#where-to-get-help" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>In an emergency, call 000 for an ambulance</li>
<li>Your GP (doctor)</li>
<li>Midwife</li>
<li>Obstetrician</li>
<li>Your hospital or birth centre</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preferences-for-giving-birth">Preferences for Giving Birth<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preferences-for-giving-birth" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preferences-for-after-the-delivery">Preferences for After the Delivery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preferences-for-after-the-delivery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<p>SAFE</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="safe-motherhood-maternal-and-neonatal-health">Safe Motherhood, Maternal and Neonatal Health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#safe-motherhood-maternal-and-neonatal-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Maternal and neonatal morbidity and mortality levels in Kenya have remained unacceptably high. The maternal mortality ratio has remained at over 400 per 100,000 live births since 1998. The neonatal mortality rate was estimated at 33 per 1,000 live births in 2003 (28 per 1,000 live births in 1998), while the perinatal mortality rate was estimated at 40 in 2003 and 45 per 1,000 live births in 1998.</p>
<p>Statistics from the 2003 KDHS indicated that nationally, only 42 per cent of births in Kenya were attended to by a skilled attendant, a figure that varied regionally and by economic status. Skilled attendance implies access to appropriately trained health providers whether in a health facility or through domiciliary care, and having access to a rapid means of referral in case of emergency. In this context, the traditional birth attendants (TBAs) are not recognised as providers of skilled care.</p>
<p>Most neonatal deaths are due to</p>
<p>60</p>
<p>infections, birth asphyxia, birth injuries, complications of prematurity and low birth weight, and birth defects. In the case of maternal deaths, most result from one or more of five "direct" obstetric complications: postpartum haemorrhage, obstructed labour/ruptured uterus, pre-eclampsia/eclampsia, puerperal sepsis, and unsafe abortion.</p>
<p>The following are key challenges to safe motherhood, maternal and neonatal health:</p>
<p>a) Inadequate access by women to RH information and to skilled care throughout the continuum of pregnancy, delivery, post-partum and post-natal periods, especially the rural and urban poor, and women living in arid and semi-arid regions, pastoral and nomadic populations and other hard to reach groups;
b) Weaknesses in the health system, including service provision and referral that negatively affect access to, quality of care, demand for and utilisation of reproductive health services;
c) Redefining the role of other community-owned resource persons (CORPs) including TBAs with regard to pregnancy, early identification and referrals of complications, post-natal care and registration of births; and
d) Inadequate access to improved care of the newborn, including facilities for resuscitation, thermal regulation, infection prevention and promotion of early and exclusive breastfeeding.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="priority-actions">Priority Actions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#priority-actions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To reduce maternal, perinatal and neonatal morbidity and mortality in Kenya, the safe motherhood component of the reproductive health programme will:</p>
<p>i. Ensure that all women, including adolescents/youth have access to reproductive health information, counselling and services;
ii. Ensure that all pregnant women, including the poor and 'hard-to-reach', have access to skilled care throughout pregnancy, delivery, postpartum, postnatal periods and care of the newborn; and that TBAs are not recognised as providers of skilled care;
iii. Increase access to both comprehensive and basic emergency obstetric care to meet minimum international standards;
iv. Remove barriers (geographic, socio-cultural, economic, legal or regulatory) that impede access to skilled care for the poor and 'hard-to-reach' women, including promotion of community midwifery</p>
<p>b) services, women- and baby-friendly services, and establishment of maternity shelters, as appropriate;</p>
<p>i. Ensure that communities are involved in measures to promote 'women- and baby-friendly' maternity services and assisting with transport;</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>61</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>ii. Ensure that referral networks across public and non-public facilities are promoted and strengthened;
iii. Strengthen the capacity of the health system at all levels for efficient and effective delivery of services for the newborn, including resuscitation, thermal regulation, infection prevention and promotion of early and exclusive breastfeeding;
iv. Strengthen the capacity of CORPs, including TBAs to enable them play designated roles such as promotion of birth-preparedness, early identification and referrals of complications, post-natal care and</p>
<p>c) registration of births; and Review all maternal and perinatal deaths and provide notification on maternal deaths.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="safe-motherhood">Safe motherhood:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#safe-motherhood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Safe motherhood is the concept or initiatives to ensure that women receive high quality care in order to achieve the optimum level of health of mother and infant.</li>
<li>Safe motherhood is designed in a way that the women is ensured of high-quality gynecological, family planning, prenatal, delivery and postpartum care.</li>
<li>Safe motherhood aims at improving maternal and child health and eliminating the probable risk that can occur.</li>
<li>Safe motherhood is required for obtaining the desired outcome of pregnancy.</li>
<li>The goal of the Safe Motherhood Program is to reduce maternal and neonatal morbidity and mortality and to improve the maternal and neonatal health through preventive and promotive activities as well as by addressing avoidable factors that cause death during pregnancy, childbirth and postpartum period</li>
<li>Safe pregnancy, safe delivery and safe birth of new born are the major components of safe motherhood. These components are achieved through the principles of safe motherhood.</li>
<li>Safe motherhood also ensures the safety of overall pregnancy and health of mother and child</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="why-safe-motherhood">Why safe motherhood?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-safe-motherhood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>In 2007 there were at least 3.2 million stillborn babies, 4 million neonatal deaths and more than half a million maternal deaths globally.</li>
<li>Every day in 2015, about 830 women died due to complications of pregnancy and child birth. Most of these could have been prevented.</li>
<li>Maternal and neonatal deaths are still high and unacceptable.</li>
<li>Over half of maternal deaths are due to preventable or treatable conditions.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>The maternal morbidity and mortality can be reduced through preventive and promotive activities and by addressing avoidable factors that cause death, which are included in safe motherhood initiatives.</li>
<li>For newborns, most deaths are due to premature birth, infections and complications of asphyxia, again all preventable or treatable conditions.</li>
</ul>
<p>Pillars of safe motherhood:</p>
<ol>
<li>Family Planning:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>FP is an important component of safe motherhood</li>
<li>It is necessary to ensure that individuals and couples have adequate information and services regarding FP</li>
<li>FP is also necessary to plan the timing, number of children, spacing between pregnancies, delay pregnancy, etc.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Antenatal Care (ANC)</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>ANC checkup is necessary to detect complications early and treat them as soon as possible</li>
<li>It is also essential to provide pregnant women with vitamin supplements, iron tablets and vaccinations so that they can have a healthy and strong pregnancy.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Obstetric and Newborn Care</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Obstetric and newborn care refers to all the care and health care level initiatives provided to the mother and newborn to reduce maternal and newborn mortality and morbidity.</li>
<li>Birth attendants should have the knowledge, skills, and equipment to perform a clean and safe delivery.</li>
<li>Moreover, emergency care for high-risk pregnancies and complications are made available to all women and newborn who need it.</li>
<li>vaccinations so that they can have a healthy and strong pregnancy.</li>
</ul>
<p>3.1 Essential Obstetric and Newborn Care (EONC):</p>
<ul>
<li>Essential obstetric and newborn care encompasses all care that is provided during pregnancy, labor, childbirth and postpartum period to prevent and manage complications.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
S
studocu
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>It is a term used to describe the elements of obstetric and newborn care needed for the management of normal and complicated pregnancy, delivery, postpartum period.</li>
</ul>
<p>Essential Obstetric and Newborn Care is differentiated into two levels:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-1-1-basic-emergency-obstetric-and-newborn-care-bemonc">3.1.1 Basic Emergency Obstetric and Newborn Care (BEmONC)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-1-1-basic-emergency-obstetric-and-newborn-care-bemonc" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It includes following signal functions (i.e., key interventions to treat/manage key causes of maternal and newborn mortality):</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-aa7db23b.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>Management of pregnancy complications by assisted vaginal delivery (using vacuum extractor or forceps)</li>
<li>Availability/administration of antibiotics</li>
<li>Availability/administration of sedatives and anticonvulsants for eclampsia</li>
<li>Availability/Administration of parenteral Uterotonics (a drug that causes contraction of uterus) like oxytocin, ergometrine, misoprostol, or prostaglandin etc.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>(Note: Ergometrine should NEVER be given to a woman with elevated blood pressure because it can precipitate an eclamptic seizure/convulsion.)</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Availability/Administration of parental drugs (for PPH, infection and pre-eclampsia and eclampsia</li>
<li>Manual removal of placenta</li>
<li>Manual removal of retained products of conception. (facilitated with a manual vacuum aspirator or dilatation &amp; curettage (D&amp;C))</li>
<li>Resuscitation of newborns (using a self-inflating bag and mask (Ambu bag) and room air).</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Availability/Administration of parenteral antibiotics to the newborn.</li>
</ul>
<p>BEmONC services are usually provided at the primary health care levels by skilled birth attendants of any cadre.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-1-2-comprehensive-emergency-obstetric-and-newborn-care-cemonc">3.1.2 Comprehensive Emergency Obstetric and Newborn Care (CEmONC):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-1-2-comprehensive-emergency-obstetric-and-newborn-care-cemonc" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It includes all the services of basic essential obstetric services along with following additional services:</p>
<ul>
<li>Cesarean section/surgery</li>
<li>Blood transfusion</li>
<li>Anesthesia</li>
<li>Umbical vein insertion and</li>
<li>Intubation of the newborn</li>
</ul>
<p>CEmONC services are basically provided at the referral hospitals by physicians, clinicians or specially trained midwives.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-postnatal-care-pnc">4. Postnatal Care (PNC)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-postnatal-care-pnc" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is necessary to ensure that postpartum care is provided to the mother and baby.</li>
<li>It includes counselling mothers about child handling, exclusive breast feeding, etc.</li>
<li>Moreover, PNC also comprises of providing awareness regarding the FP, and managing the danger signs and symptoms seen in both mother and child.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-post-abortion-care">5. Post abortion Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-post-abortion-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is necessary to prevent complications of abortion.</li>
<li>Post abortion care helps to identify/detect if there are any complications of abortion.</li>
<li>Useful to refer other reproductive health problems when necessary.</li>
<li>An essential element of post abortion care services is providing the woman with a family planning method before she leaves the facility.</li>
<li>It also provides counselling and awareness about different family planning methods.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="essential-elements-of-post-abortion-care-pac-services-are">Essential Elements of Post Abortion Care (PAC) services are:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#essential-elements-of-post-abortion-care-pac-services-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Emergency treatment of incomplete abortion and potentially life-threatening complications.</li>
<li>Post abortion family planning counseling and services.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-std-hiv-aids-control">6. STD/HIV/AIDS Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-std-hiv-aids-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="direct-cause-for-the-majority-of-maternal-deaths-are">Direct cause for the majority of maternal deaths are:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#direct-cause-for-the-majority-of-maternal-deaths-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-severe-bleeding">1. Severe bleeding<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-severe-bleeding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-infections">2. Infections<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-infections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<li>Includes infection of the uterus, tubes, urinary system and fetal infection.</li>
<li>Also caused due to unhygienic delivery site and practice</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-high-blood-pressure-during-pregnancy">3. High blood pressure during pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-high-blood-pressure-during-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Includes pre-eclampsia and eclampsia</li>
