<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="4-complications-from-delivery">4. Complications from delivery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-complications-from-delivery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Several complications can arise during the pregnancy</li>
<li>Teenage pregnancy, advanced maternal age, parity, etc and many other factors can cause complications</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="5-unsafe-abortion">5. Unsafe abortion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-unsafe-abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Common cause of maternal death</li>
<li>Unsafe abortions are high in countries where abortion is not legalized</li>
</ul>
<p>These factors contribute to nearly 75% of all maternal deaths.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Indirect causes:</p>
<p>a) 3 delays</p>
<p>Three delays usually refer to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Delay in the decision to seek care (seeking care)</li>
<li>Delay arrival at a health facility (reaching care) and</li>
<li>Delay in obtaining the adequate treatment (receiving care)</li>
</ul>
<p>These delays contribute to increase the complication in pregnancy. However, these delays are determined by the educational status, financial status, accessibility of health care and services, etc.</p>
<p>b) Accessibility</p>
<ul>
<li>Health services and facilities are still not available in every knock and corner of many countries</li>
<li>Reaching health facility is often riskier in some places</li>
<li>Lack of accessibility promotes the delay</li>
</ul>
<p>c) Poverty</p>
<ul>
<li>Poverty is the other important factor contributing to maternal deaths</li>
<li>People of rural areas do not fancy health services</li>
<li>Seeking health services often is not the priority to those people who have to worry about hands to mouth</li>
</ul>
<p>d) Cultural practices</p>
<ul>
<li>Traditional practices often prevent individual from seeking health care</li>
<li>Cultural practices also determine the care given to pregnant women, food practices, etc.,</li>
<li>Unsafe abortion is also an example of cultural practices.</li>
</ul>

<p>2.5 POSTNATAL CARE:</p>
<p>It the care given to the mother and newborn from one hour after delivery upto 6 weeks post-delivery. During postnatal care always give equal attention and care for both the mother and the new born.</p>
<p>Objectives of Postnatal Care:</p>
<ul>
<li>To access the health status of the mother and institute effective therapy to rectify the defect if any Medical disorders like Diabetes mellitus should be reassessed.</li>
<li>To ascertain outcome of each pregnancy and follow up of the survival of the newborn.</li>
<li>To detect and treat the earliest any gynecological condition arising out obstetric legacy.</li>
<li>To note the progress of the baby including Immunization schedule for the infant.</li>
<li>To promote physical well-being of the mother and the baby.</li>
<li>Promote and support on breast-feeding.</li>
<li>Guidance on Family Planning.</li>
<li>Provide emotional support.</li>
<li>Health education on weaning and food preparation.</li>
<li>Discuss about menstruation (when it will restart) and when to start sexual relation (this point is usually overlooked in post natal clinics).</li>
</ul>
<p>Components of postnatal care:</p>
<p>1- History</p>
<ul>
<li>a) Any complications during pregnancy or labour.</li>
<li>b) Any abnormal symptoms or signs of complications, (hemorrhage, infections and eclampsia)</li>
<li>Vaginal bleeding, normally it is blood in the few days after delivery, later it becomes brownish then pink, and it becomes colorless only by 24th day.</li>
<li>Bad smelling vaginal discharge.</li>
<li>Pain or tenderness in the abdomen or breast.</li>
<li>Fever.</li>
<li>c) Diet What she is eating.</li>
</ul>
<p>68</p>
<p>2- physical examination</p>
<ul>
<li>The Mother</li>
<li>Measuring temperature, blood pressure</li>
<li>Abdomen for swelling, distended bladder, for cesarean incision and for determining the size and firmness (involution) of the uterus.</li>
<li>Perineum for swelling, discharge, tears episiotomies.</li>
<li>NB No vaginal examination should be performed early in puerperium except when it is absolutely indicated.</li>
<li>breast for cracked nipples, engorgement or abscess.</li>
<li>Leg for thrombosis.</li>
<li>Checking for signs of anemia.</li>
<li>The newborn for vital signs, umbilical stump, suckling power, respiratory distress (cyanosis), tremors, convulsion and jaundice. Ask about vomiting, constipation or anuria</li>
</ul>
<p>3- Give the proper treatment if needed, give 200 000 IU of vitamin A orally iron</p>
<p>4- Refer the post-partum cases requiring special treatment.</p>
<p>5- Record the finding on the maternal card.</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Health education.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>The key messages that should be covered are the followings</li>
</ul>
<p>1- Avoid puerperal infection</p>
<ul>
<li>Personal hygiene particularly that after urination and defecation</li>
<li>No person with any upper respiratory tract infection or hand infection should be attending during exposure of the genitalia.</li>
</ul>
<p>2- Care for the episiotomy or first degree perineal tear</p>
<ul>
<li>The woman has to be trained to clean the wound daily in the morning and each time after she passes any urine or stools using warm water and soap.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
69
studocu
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>3- Sleep and rest</p>
<ul>
<li>The mother should have periods of rest</li>
<li>Gradual return to household duties is advisable starting by the end of the first week. She should avoid any strenuous activity for about 4 weeks.</li>
</ul>
<p>4- Diet</p>
<ul>
<li>She should be aware that all her nutritional needs are increased during the first six months of lactation together with fluid intake iron supplementation.</li>
</ul>
<p>5- Advice and counseling on breastfeeding</p>
<ul>
<li>The woman should be instructed about:</li>
<li>Advantages of breast feeding</li>
<li>Importance of early initiation of breast feeding (within ½ -1 hr)</li>
<li>Encourage breast feeding on demands.</li>
<li>Personal hygiene after feeding. Only water is recommended for washing</li>
<li>nipples and allowed to dry in air after feeding and then covered with</li>
<li>clean pads. Drying agents as boric acid alcohol must be avoided.</li>
</ul>
<p>2.6: ABORTION:</p>
<ul>
<li>Abortion is the termination of pregnancy by any means, resulting in expulsion of an immature nonviable foetus of less than 28 weeks.</li>
<li>Abortion can be early or late depending on gestation, early up to 12 weeks gestation and late between 13-28 weeks gestation.</li>
<li>It could be induced or spontaneous.</li>
<li>Three consecutive abortions would be termed; habitual abortion.</li>
<li>The frequency of spontaneous abortions is 12 to 15%.</li>
<li>The frequency of habitual abortion is about 0.4 to 0.8%.</li>
<li>Habitual abortion affects 2 to 5% of childless couples.</li>
<li>75% of spontaneous abortions occur before the 16th week of gestation and 62% before 12 weeks.</li>
<li>The incidence of subclinical abortions is estimated at 8%.</li>
<li>A few risk factors have been elucidated:</li>
<li>The risk increases with age (OR=2.3 after the age of 30).</li>
</ul>
<p>70</p>
<ul>
<li>Past history: risk after one abortion is 8%, 40% after 3 abortions and 60% after 4 abortions.</li>
<li>Ethnic origin and psychological factors.</li>
<li>Parity, history of voluntary induced abortion, medically assisted conception, contraceptive method, tobacco consumption do not seem to play any significant role in spontaneous abortions (J Lansac).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-abortion">CLASSIFICATION OF ABORTION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Threatening abortion</li>
<li>Inevitable abortion</li>
<li>Incomplete abortion</li>
<li>Complete abortion</li>
<li>Missed abortion</li>
<li>Septic abortion</li>
<li>Criminal abortion</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-abortion">CAUSES OF ABORTION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Chromosomal causes (genetic) are most frequent, about 70% within the first 6 weeks, 50% before 10 weeks, 5% after 12 weeks.</p>
<ul>
<li>Could be: -errors during gametogenesis, non disjunction in paternal or maternal meiosis, resulting in monosomy (15%), trisomy (54%) or a double trisomy (3%).</li>
<li>Infections are the second cause of abortions, representing about 15% of the cases.</li>
<li>Common viruses like the mumps virus, influenzae, varicella and herpes zoster have no proven risk.</li>
<li>Cervical incompetence, acquired (D/C, deliveries, conization, synechiae operations etc.) or congenital, causes 30% of 2nd trimester abortions.hypoplasia and hypotrophy, leiomyomas, synechiae or congenital malformations.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="metabolic-and-vascular-causes">Metabolic and vascular causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#metabolic-and-vascular-causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Diabetes: risk doubles if poorly controlled.</li>
<li>HTN increases the risk.</li>
<li>Tobacco consumption.</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>Chronic renal diseases.</li>
<li>Disseminated lupus erythematosis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-of-abortion">COMPLICATIONS OF ABORTION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>Septicaemia</li>
<li>Bacteraemia shock with rigors, nausea, vomiting, diarrhoea, hypotension, confusion, delirium and coma</li>
<li>Renal failure</li>
<li>Secondary infertility</li>
<li>Death</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-a-woman-with-abortion">MANAGEMENT OF A WOMAN WITH ABORTION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-a-woman-with-abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="general-management-of-abortion">General management of abortion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-management-of-abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>The woman with abortion must be admitted to gynaecological ward for close observation and treatment</li>
<li>History taking to obtain possible aetiological factors together with details of bleeding, pain and products of conception expelled</li>
<li>Perform a full physical examination</li>
<li>Check and record vital signs i.e. temperature, pulse, respiration and blood pressure</li>
<li>Observe aseptic technique when performing vaginal examinations</li>
<li>Provide pads to observe severity of blood loss</li>
<li>Put up intravenous fluids if the woman is bleeding severely i.e. normal saline, ringers lactate</li>
<li>If necessary Check Hb, grouping and cross matching and arrange for blood donor</li>
<li>Give antibiotics to treat infection in case of septic abortion</li>
<li>MVA is the method of choice for the management of incomplete or inevitable</li>
</ul>
<p>Abortion for gestation of 14 weeks or less, because it has fewer complications compared to curettage.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit-3-family-planning">UNIT 3: FAMILY PLANNING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-3-family-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Family planning involves planning the number, frequency and timing of pregnancy. In other words, it is engaging in activities aimed at regulating the number and spacing of children in the family through the practice of contraception or other methods of birth control.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="purpose-of-family-planning">Purpose of family planning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#purpose-of-family-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Raising a child requires significant amounts of resources: time, social, financial and environmental. Planning can ensure that resources are available.</li>
<li>To improve the health of the mother and the child</li>
<li>HelppreventHIV/AIDS</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="family-planning-methods">Family Planning Methods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#family-planning-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Methods of contraception include oral contraceptive pills, implants, injectables, patches, vaginal rings, Intra uterine devices, condoms, male and female sterilization, lactational amenorrhea methods, withdrawal and fertility awareness-based methods. These methods have different mechanisms of action and effectiveness in preventing unintended pregnancy. Effectiveness of methods is measured by the number of pregnancies per 100 women using the method per year.</p>
<p>Methods are classified by their effectiveness as commonly used into: Very effective (0–0.9 pregnancies per 100 women); Effective (1–9 pregnancies per 100</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>women); Moderately effective (10-19 pregnancies per 100 women); Less effective (20 or more pregnancies per 100 women)</p>
<p>Criteria for ideal contraceptive</p>
<ul>
<li>It should be safe for use, means free from any kind of side effects</li>
<li>It should be reliable</li>
<li>It should be easy to administer and convenient</li>
<li>It should be cost effective</li>
<li>It should be culturally feasible and acceptable</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-oral-pills">A. ORAL PILLS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-oral-pills" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>COMBINED ORAL CONTRACEPTIVES (COCs) pills</p>
<p>E.g., Microgynon or Femiplan</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-it-is">What it is?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-it-is" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Pills that contain low doses of two hormones (oestrogen and progestin) in it like the natural hormones in the woman's body (progesterone and oestrogen).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-it-works">How it works<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-it-works" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The two hormones (oestrogen and progestin) works by preventing release of egg (ovum) from ovaries (ovulation) each month. It also thickens cervical mucus and blocks sperm from meeting egg in the uterine tube.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-effective">How effective?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-effective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Effectiveness depends on the user: risk of pregnancy is greatest when a woman starts a new pill pack 3 or more days late; or misses 3 or more pills near the beginning or end of a pill pack.</li>
<li>As commonly used, about 8 pregnancies per 100 women using COCs over the first year. This means that 92 of every 100 women using COCs will not become pregnant.</li>
<li>hen no pill-taking mistakes are made, less than one pregnancy per 100 women using COCs over the past year (3 per 1000 women).</li>
<li>No delay in return of fertility when COC used is stopped.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="who-can-use-it">Who can use it?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-can-use-it" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Women of child bearing age</li>
<li>Have or have not had children</li>
<li>Are of any age including adolescents and women over 40 years old</li>
<li>Have just had an abortion or miscarriage</li>
<li>Smoke cigarette if under 35 years of age</li>
<li>Have anemia now or had in the past</li>
<li>Have varicose veins</li>
<li>Are infected with HIV whether or not on retroviral therapy, unless that therapy includes ritonavir</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="who-cannot-use">Who cannot use?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-cannot-use" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Women who are pregnant</li>
<li>Breastfeeding mothers with babies less than six months old</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-to-use">How to use<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-to-use" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<p>Take one pill every day at the same time</p>
<p>When you finish a pack of 21 pills, rest for seven days and start a new pack on the eighth day. If using 28-pill pack start a new pack the next day</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="if-you-miss-a-pill">If you miss a pill<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#if-you-miss-a-pill" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>If you miss 1 or 2 pills; take missed pill as soon as you remember and continue taking one pill every day. It is alright to take 2 pills at the same time</li>
<li>If you miss more than 3 days of pills in a row or start a pack 3 days late, use condoms or abstain for 7 days and keep taking pills</li>
<li>If you miss 3 pills or more in week 3, SKIP the remaining pills and start a new pack; use condom or abstain for the next 7 days if missed any of the last 7 pills (iron pills in a 28- pill pack), discard the missed pills and continue taking</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-to-expect">What to expect<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-to-expect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Change in bleeding patterns (irregular, light, or absence of periods)</li>
<li>Some women have stomach upset or mild headaches that go away after the first three Months</li>
<li>Breast tenderness and weight gain</li>
<li>Some women may experience nausea (ask them to take pill with food)</li>
<li>Mood changes</li>
<li>Does not disrupt existing pregnancy</li>
<li>Use condoms for protection against STI’s including HIV.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-of-the-pill">Advantages of the pill<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-the-pill" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Safe</li>
<li>Effective when a pill is taken every day</li>
<li>Less monthly bleeding and cramps</li>
<li>Can be stopped any time if the woman desires pregnancy</li>
<li>Can sometimes be used to treat period pain, heavy periods,</li>

<ul>
<li>Does not interfere with sex.</li>
<li>Can be provided by trained non-technical staff e.g.,</li>
<li>Community Health Workers/Community Based Distributors (CHV/CBDs)</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages">Disadvantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Failure rate increases if the intake is irregular</li>
<li>Minor side effects like dizziness, nausea, vomiting, headache, weight gain etc.</li>
<li>Increases the risk of heart problems if the woman is already at risk</li>
<li>May increase the risk of cervical cancer and gall bladder disease</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="known-health-benefits">Known health benefits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#known-health-benefits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Help protect against:</li>
<li>Risks of pregnancy</li>
<li>Cancer of the lining of the uterus (endometrial cancer)</li>
<li>Cancer of the ovary</li>
<li>Symptomatic pelvic inflammatory disease</li>
<li>May help protect against:</li>
<li>Ovarian cysts</li>
<li>Iron-deficiency anemia</li>
<li>Reduce:</li>
<li>Menstrual cramps</li>
<li>Menstrual bleeding problems</li>
<li>Ovulation pain</li>
<li>Excess hair on face or body</li>
<li>Symptoms of polycystic ovarian syndrome (irregular bleeding, acne, excess hair on face or body)</li>
<li>Symptoms of endometriosis (pelvic pain, irregular bleeding)</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="correcting-misunderstanding">Correcting Misunderstanding<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#correcting-misunderstanding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Combined oral contraceptives:</li>
<li>Do not build up in a woman’s body.</li>
<li>Women do not need a “rest” from taking COCs.</li>
<li>Must be taken every day, whether or not a woman has sex that day.</li>
<li>Do not make women infertile.</li>
<li>Do not cause birth defects or multiple births.</li>
<li>Do not change women’s sexual behavior.</li>
<li>Do not collect in the stomach. Instead, the pill dissolves each day.</li>
<li>Do not disrupt an existing pregnancy.</li>
</ul>
<p>PROGESTIN-ONLY PILLS (POPs)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c2fc5575">Also called “minipills”<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c2fc5575" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-it-is">What it is<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-it-is" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pills that contain very low doses of a progestin like the natural progesterone hormone in a woman’s body.</p>
<p>Safe and most effective when used while breastfeeding less than 6 months after delivery since they do not contain oestrogen</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-pop-work">How POP work?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-pop-work" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Work primarily by;</p>
<ul>
<li>Thickening the cervical mucus thus, blocks sperms from reaching the egg (ovum)</li>
<li>Disrupting the menstrual cycle, including preventing the release of eggs from ovary (suppresses ovulation)</li>
<li>Making the lining of the uterus thin</li>
<li>Slowing down the egg (ovum) in the fallopian tube</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-effective">How effective?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-effective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><strong>Effectiveness depends on the user:</strong> for women who have monthly bleeding (monthly period), risk of getting pregnant is greatest if pills are taken late or missed completely. Less effective for women who are not breastfeeding.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="breastfeeding">Breastfeeding:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#breastfeeding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As commonly used, about 1 pregnancy per 100 women using POPs over the first year. This means that 99 of 100 women will not become pregnant</p>
<p>When pills are taken every day, less than 1 pregnancy per 100 women using POPs over the first year (3 per 1000 women)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="less-effective-for-women-not-breastfeeding">Less effective for women not breastfeeding:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#less-effective-for-women-not-breastfeeding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As commonly used, about 3 to 10 pregnancies per 100 women using POPs over the first year. This means that 90 to 97 of every 100 women will not become pregnant.</p>
<p>When pills are taken every day at the same time, less than one pregnancy per 100 women using POPs over the first year (9 per 1000 women).</p>
<p>There is no delay in return of fertility after POPs are stopped.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="who-can-use">Who can use?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-can-use" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Women of child bearing age</li>
<li>Women who are breastfeeding and baby is less than six months</li>
<li>Women who can follow a daily routine of pill taking</li>
<li>Have or have not had children</li>
</ul>
<p>79</p>
<p>○ Are of any age including adolescents and women over 40 years of age
○ Have just have an abortion, miscarriage or ectopic pregnancy
○ Smoke cigarettes irrespective of the woman's age or number of cigarettes smoked
○ Have anemia now or had anemia
○ Have varicose veins
○ Are infected with HIV, whether or not on antiretroviral therapy, unless that therapy includes ritovir</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="who-cannot-use">Who cannot use?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-cannot-use" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>○ Women who are breastfeeding infants more than six months of age
○ Women with breast lumps or breast cancer
○ Women with yellow discoloration of eyes
○ Women with blood clots in their legs or lungs
○ Women taking drugs for TB, epilepsy, or HIV</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-to-use">How to use<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-to-use" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>○ If breastfeeding, can start 4 weeks after childbirth
○ Take one pill at the same time every day
○ When you finish a pack of pills, start a new pack the next day</p>
<p>✓ Late taking pill, for women who are breastfeeding:
○ Take a pill as soon as you remember, and continue taking pills
✓ Late taking pill, for women who are not breastfeeding:
○ If you take a pill more than three hours late, use condoms for the next 2 days and keep taking pills</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-to-expect-if-not-breastfeeding">What to expect, if not breastfeeding<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-to-expect-if-not-breastfeeding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Changes in monthly bleeding including irregular bleeding, spotting, heavier bleeding or no monthly bleeding, are common, safe and not life threatening</li>
<li>Nausea and dizziness</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>Do not cause a breastfeeding woman’s milk to dry up.</li>
<li>Must be taken every day, whether or not a woman has sex that day.</li>
<li>Do not make women infertile.</li>

<p><strong>Note:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>These effects are temporary and will disappear with time. If it bothers you or persists refer to the nearest health facility</li>

<li>Use condoms for protection against STIs including HIV/AIDS</li>
<li>Emergency contraceptive pills</li>

<p>EMERGENCY CONTRACEPTIVE PILLS (ECPs)</p>
<p>Also called “morning after pills” or postcoital contraceptives</p>
<p><strong>What it is</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Pills that contain a progestin alone, or a progestin and an oestrogen together, hormones like the natural hormones in a woman’s body.</li>
<li>Pills used to prevent pregnancy within 120 hours (5 days) after unprotected sex. The earlier they are taken the better</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>When to take them</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>As soon as possible after unprotected sex. The sooner ECPs are taken after unprotected sex, the better they prevent pregnancy.</li>
<li>Can help to prevent pregnancy when taken any time up to 5 days after unprotected sex</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>How Effective?</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>If 100 women each had sex once during the second or third week of the menstrual cycle without using contraception, 8 would likely become pregnant.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>If all 100 women used ulipristal acetate ECPs, fewer than one woman would likely become pregnant.
If all 100 women used progestin-only ECPs, one woman would likely become pregnant.
If all 100 women used combined estrogen and progestin ECPs, 2 women would likely become pregnant</p>
<ul>
<li>Return of fertility after taking ECPs: No delay. A woman can become pregnant immediately after taking ECPs. Taking ECPs prevents pregnancy only from acts of sex that took place in the 5 days before. They will not protect a woman from pregnancy from acts of sex more than 24 hours after she takes ECPs. To stay protected from pregnancy, women must begin to use another contraceptive method.</li>
</ul>
<p>Protection against sexually transmitted infections (STIs): None</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-it-works">How it works<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-it-works" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Work primarily by preventing or delaying the release of eggs from the ovaries (ovulation). Thus, no egg can be fertilized. They do not work if the woman is already pregnant</li>
<li>They may also work by changing the lining of the womb that may prevent implantation of a fertilized egg.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-pills-can-be-used-as-emergency-contraceptive-pills">What pills can be used as emergency contraceptive pills?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-pills-can-be-used-as-emergency-contraceptive-pills" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A special ECPs product with levonorgestrel only, or oestrogen and levonorgestrel combined or ulipristal acetate</li>
<li>Progestin-only pills with levonorgestrel or nogestrel</li>
<li>Combined oral contraceptives with oestrogen and a progestin-levonorgestrel, norgestrel, or norethindrone</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="it-can-be-taken-in-the-following-situations">It can be taken in the following situations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#it-can-be-taken-in-the-following-situations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="avoid-unnecessary-procedures">Avoid Unnecessary Procedures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#avoid-unnecessary-procedures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-injectable-contraceptives">B. INJECTABLE CONTRACEPTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-injectable-contraceptives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-it-is">What it is<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-it-is" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Injections given every 1 month (CIC), 2 months (NETEN) or 3 months (DMPA)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="depo-provera">Depo Provera<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#depo-provera" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-it-is">What it is<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-it-is" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>The injectable contraceptives depot medroxyprogesterone acetate (DMPA) and norethisterone enanthate (NET-EN) each contain a progestin like the natural hormone progesterone in a woman's body. (In contrast, monthly injectables contain both estrogen and progestin.</li>
<li>Do not contain estrogen, and so can be used throughout breastfeeding and by women who cannot use methods with estrogen.</li>
<li>DMPA, the most widely used progestin-only injectable, is also known as "the shot," "the jab," the injection, Depo, Depo-Provera, Megestron, and Petogen.</li>
<li>Injectable contraceptive given every 3 months. Given by injection into the muscle (intramuscular injection) either in the deltoid muscle of the arm or buttocks. The hormone is then released slowly into the bloodstream.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-effective">How effective?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-effective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Effectiveness depends on getting injections regularly: risk of pregnancy is greatest when a woman misses an injection. It is 97% effective.</li>
<li>As commonly used, about three pregnancies per 100 women using progestin-only injectables over the first year. This means that 97 of every 100 women using injectables will not become pregnant</li>
<li>When women have injections on time, less than 1 pregnancy per 100 women using progestin-only injectables over the first year (3 per 1000 women)</li>
<li>Return of fertility after injections are stopped. An average of about 4 months for DMPA and 1 month longer for NET-EN than with most other methods.</li>
<li>Protection against sexually transmitted infections (STIs): None</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-it-is">What it is<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-it-is" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Plastic pouch inserted into the vagina before sex</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-f3d84f2f.jpeg" alt="img-19.jpeg"></p>
<p>Sheaths, or linings, that fit loosely inside a woman's vagina, made of thin, transparent, soft plastic film.</p>
<ul>
<li>Have flexible rings at both ends</li>
<li>One ring at the closed end helps to insert the condom</li>
<li>The ring at the open end holds part of the condom outside the vagina</li>
</ul>
<p>Female condoms are made of various materials, such as latex, polyurethane, and nitrile.
Work by forming a barrier that keeps sperm out of the vagina, preventing pregnancy. Also helps to keep infections in semen, on the penis, or in the vagina from infecting the other partner.</p>

<p>Effectiveness depends on the user: Risk of pregnancy or sexually transmitted infection (STI) is greatest when female condoms are not used with every act of sex. Few pregnancies or infections occur due to incorrect use, slips, or breaks.</p>
<p>Protection against pregnancy:</p>
<ul>
<li>As commonly used, about 21 pregnancies per 100 women using female condoms over the first year. This means that 79 of every 100 women using female condoms will not become pregnant.</li>
<li>When used correctly with every act of sex, about 5 pregnancies per 100 women using female condoms over the first year.</li>
</ul>

<p>Protection against HIV and other STIs:</p>
<ul>
<li>Female condoms reduce the risk of infection with STIs, including HIV, when used correctly with every act of sex</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>Cannot get lost in the woman's body.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="male-condom">MALE CONDOM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#male-condom" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-it-is">What it is<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-it-is" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A thin rubber covering that fits over the erect penis</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-a127cc04.jpeg" alt="img-20.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>Also called rubbers, “raincoats,” “umbrellas,” skins, prophylactics and preservatives; known by many different brand names.</li>
<li>Most are made of thin latex rubber. Male condoms also are made from other materials, including polyurethane, polyisoprene, lambskin, and nitrile.</li>
<li>Work by forming a barrier that keeps sperm out of the vagina, preventing pregnancy. Also keep infections in semen, on the penis, or in the vagina from infecting the other partner</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="how-effective">How effective<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-effective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>Effectiveness depends on the user:</strong> Risk of pregnancy or sexually transmitted infection (STI) is greatest when condoms are not used with every act of sex. Very few pregnancies or infections occur due to incorrect use, slips, or breaks.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>97</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Protection against pregnancy:</p>
<ul>
<li>As commonly used, about 13 pregnancies per 100 women whose partners use male condoms over the first year. This means that 87 of every 100 women whose partners use male condoms will not become pregnant.</li>
<li>When used correctly with every act of sex, about 2 pregnancies per 100 women whose partners use male condoms over the first year.</li>
</ul>
<p>Return of fertility after use of condoms is stopped: No delay</p>
<p>Protection against HIV and other STIs:</p>
<ul>
<li>Male condoms significantly reduce the risk of becoming infected with HIV when used correctly with every act of vaginal or anal sex</li>
<li>When used consistently and correctly, condom use prevents 80% to 95% of HIV transmission that would have occurred without condoms.</li>
<li>Condoms reduce the risk of becoming infected with many STIs when used consistently and correctly during vaginal or anal sex.</li>
<li>Protect best against STIs spread by discharge, such as HIV, gonorrhea, and chlamydia.</li>
<li>Also protect against STIs spread by skin-to-skin contact, such as herpes and human papillomavirus.</li>
</ul>
<p>Who can use condoms?</p>
<ul>
<li>Men who wish to participate actively in Family Planning</li>
<li>Couples needing a backup method (e.g., for missed pills)</li>
<li>Couples who do not have sex frequently and do not need continual protection</li>
<li>Couples who want protection from STIs including HIV</li>
</ul>
<p>Who should not use condoms?</p>
<ul>
<li>Couples who cannot use condoms consistently and correctly</li>
<li>Those allergic to rubber (does not apply to female condoms which are made of plastic)</li>
</ul>

<p>Some practices can increase the risk that will make condom break and should be avoided.</p>
<ul>
<li>Do not unroll the condom first and then try to put it on the penis.</li>
<li>Do not use lubricants with an oil base. These lubricants can damage latex.</li>
<li>Do not use a condom if the color is uneven or changed.</li>
<li>Do not use a condom that feels brittle, dried out, or very sticky.</li>
<li>Do not reuse condoms.</li>
<li>Do not have dry sex.</li>
<li>Do not use more than one condom at the same time.</li>
<li>Do not use a male and female condom at the same time</li>
<li>Also, do not use the same condom when switching between different penetrative sex acts, such as from anal to vaginal sex. This can transfer bacteria that can cause infection.</li>
</ul>
<p>Advantages</p>
<ul>
<li>Can be effective if used correctly</li>
<li>Provide protection against STI and HIV</li>
<li>Easy to use</li>
<li>Disposable</li>
<li>No medical supervision is required</li>
</ul>
<p>Disadvantages</p>
<ul>
<li>Must use for every sex act</li>
<li>Requires partners cooperation</li>
<li>If not used correctly, it may slip or get tear of and the semen get spilled into the vagina</li>
<li>In some cases, an individual maybe allergic to the rubber</li>
<li>Some people may not enjoy sex because of interference with the sensation.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-is-the-diaphragm">What is the diaphragm?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-the-diaphragm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-2873280d.jpeg" alt="img-22.jpeg"></p>
<p>☐ A soft latex cup that covers the cervix. Plastic and silicone diaphragms may also be available.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The rim contains a firm, flexible spring that keeps the diaphragm in place.
Used with spermicidal cream, jelly, or foam to improve effectiveness.
Most diaphragms come in different sizes and require fitting by a specifically trained provider. A one-size-fits-all diaphragm is becoming available. It does not require seeing a provider for fitting.
Works by blocking sperm from entering the cervix; spermicide kills or disables sperm. Both keep sperm from meeting an egg.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-effective">How effective?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-effective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Effectiveness depends on the user: Risk of pregnancy is greatest when the diaphragm with spermicide is not used with every act of sex.</p>
<p>As commonly used, about 17 pregnancies per 100 women using the diaphragm with spermicide over the first year. This means that 83 of every 100 women using the diaphragm will not become pregnant.
When used correctly with every act of sex, about 16 pregnancies per 100 women using the diaphragm with spermicide over the first year.</p>
<p>Return of fertility after use of the diaphragm is stopped: No delay</p>
<p>Protection against STIs: May provide some protection against certain STIs but should not be relied on for STI prevention</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="ii-chemical-barrier-methods">ii. Chemical barrier methods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-chemical-barrier-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>These methods usually kill sperm and through this actions, chemical contraceptives help in preventing the pregnancy. They include;</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="spermicides">SPERMICIDES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spermicides" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-are-spermicides">What are spermicides<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-spermicides" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Sperm-killing substances inserted deep in the vagina, near the cervix, before sex.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Nonoxynol-9 is most widely used.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Others include benzalkonium chloride, chlorhexidine, menfegol, octoxynol-9, and sodium docusate.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Available in foaming tablets, melting or foaming suppositories, cans of pressurized foam, melting film, jelly, and cream.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Jellies, creams, and foam from cans can be used alone, with a diaphragm, or with condoms.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Films, suppositories, foaming tablets, or foaming suppositories can be used alone or with condoms.</p>
</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-it-works">How it works<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-it-works" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ Work by causing the membrane of sperm cells to break, killing them or slowing their movement. This keeps sperm from meeting an egg.
☑ Chemicals in the spermicide, such as nonoxynol -9 prevent sperm from entering the uterus.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-effective-is-spermicides">How effective is spermicides<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-effective-is-spermicides" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><strong>Effectiveness depends on the user:</strong> Risk of pregnancy is greatest when spermicides are not used with every act of sex.</p>
<ul>
<li>One of the least effective family planning methods.</li>
<li>As commonly used, about 21 pregnancies per 100 women using spermicides over the first year. This means that 79 of every 100 women using spermicides will not become pregnant.</li>
<li>When used correctly with every act of sex, about 16 pregnancies per 100 women using spermicides over the first year.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Return of fertility after spermicides are stopped:</strong> No delay</p>
<p><strong>Protection against sexually transmitted infections (STIs):</strong> None (Does not protect against STIs). Frequent use of nonoxynol-9 may increase risk of HIV infection</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="who-can-use-and-cannot-use-spermicide">Who can use and cannot use spermicide?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-can-use-and-cannot-use-spermicide" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><strong>Who can use?</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>All women can safely use spermicide</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Who cannot use spermicide?</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Are at high risk for HIV infection</li>
<li>Have HIV infection</li>
<li>Women who are at high risk for HIV infection or who have HIV should use another method</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-to-use-spermicides">How to use spermicides<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-to-use-spermicides" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><strong>Explaining how to use spermicides</strong></p>
<p>108</p>
<p>|  Give spermicides | • Give as much spermicide as possible
—even as much as a year's supply, if available.  |
| --- | --- |
|  Explain how to insert spermicide into the vagina | 1. Check the expiration date and avoid using spermicides past their expiration date.
• Wash hands with mild soap and clean water, if possible.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Foam or cream: Shake cans of foam hard. Squeeze spermicide from the can or tube into a plastic applicator. Insert the applicator deep into the vagina, near the cervix, and push the plunger.</li>
</ol>
<p>Tablets, suppositories, jellies: Insert the spermicide deep into the vagina, near the cervix, with an applicator or with fingers.
Film: Fold film in half and insert with fingers that are dry (or else the film will stick to the fingers and not the cervix).  |
|  Explain when to insert spermicide into the vagina | • Foam or cream: Any time less than one hour before sex.
• Tablets, suppositories, jellies, film: Between 10 minutes and one hour before sex, depending on type.  |
|  Explain about multiple acts of sex | • Insert additional spermicide before each act of vaginal sex.  |</p>

<p>Do not wash the vagina (douche) after sex</p>
<ul>
<li>Douching is not recommended because it will wash away the spermicide and also increase the risk of sexually transmitted infections.</li>
<li>If you must douche, wait for at least 6 hours after sex before doing so.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="known-health-risks">Known health risks<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#known-health-risks" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="correcting-misunderstandings">Correcting Misunderstandings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#correcting-misunderstandings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Spermicides:</li>
<li>Do not reduce vaginal secretions or make women bleed during sex.</li>
<li>Do not cause cervical cancer or birth defects.</li>
<li>Do not protect against STIs.</li>
<li>Do not change men's or women's sex drive or reduce sexual pleasure for most men.</li>
<li>Do not stop women's monthly bleeding.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-implants">C. IMPLANTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-implants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-are-implants">What are implants<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-implants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Small plastic rods or capsules, each about the size of a matchstick, that release a progestin like the natural hormone progesterone in a woman's body.</li>
<li>A specifically trained provider performs a minor surgical procedure to place the implant under the skin on the side on the inside of a woman's upper arm.</li>
<li>Do not contain estrogen, and so can be used throughout breastfeeding and by women who cannot use methods with estrogen.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="many-types-of-implants">Many types of implants:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#many-types-of-implants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Jadelle: 2 rods, effective for 5 year</li>
<li>Implanon: 1 rod, effective for 3 years</li>
</ul>

<p>Thickening cervical mucus (this blocks sperm from meeting an egg)
Disrupting the menstrual cycle, including preventing release of eggs from ovaries (ovulation).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-effective">How Effective<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-effective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="one-of-the-most-effective-and-long-lasting-method">One of the most effective and long-lasting method?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#one-of-the-most-effective-and-long-lasting-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Less than 1 pregnancy per 100 woman using implants over the first year (5 per 10,000 women). This means that 9,995 of every 10,000 women using implants will not become pregnant.</p>
<p>A small risk of pregnancy remains beyond the first year of use and continues as long as the woman in using implants:</p>
<ul>
<li>Over 5 years of jadelle use: about 1 pregnancy per 100 women</li>
<li>Over 3 years of implanon use: Less than 1 pregnancy per 100 women (1 per 1,000 women).</li>
<li>Over 7 years of Norplant use: about 2 pregnancies per 100 women.</li>
</ul>
<p>Jadelle, Sino-implant (II), and Norplant implants start to lose effectiveness sooner for heavier women.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>For women weighing 80 kg or more, jadelle, sino-implant (II) and Norplant become less effective after 4 years of use.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>For women weighing 70-79 kg, Norplant becomes less effective after 5 years of use. These users may want to replace their implants sooner.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Return of fertility after implant are removed: No delay</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Protection against sexually transmitted infection (STI): None</p>
</li>
</ul>
