<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="intrauterine-devices-iuds">INTRAUTERINE DEVICES (IUDs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intrauterine-devices-iuds" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-copper-bearing-intrauterine-device-what-is-the-intrauterine-device">a) COPPER-BEARING INTRAUTERINE DEVICE What is the intrauterine device?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-copper-bearing-intrauterine-device-what-is-the-intrauterine-device" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>The copper-bearing intrauterine device (IUD) is a small, flexible plastic frame with copper sleeves or wire around it. A specifically trained health care provider inserts it into a woman's uterus through her vagina and cervix.</li>
<li>Almost all types of IUDs have one or two strings, or threads, tied to them.</li>
<li>The strings hang through the cervix into the vagina.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-it-works">How it works<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-it-works" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Copper wire coiled around the device produces an inflammatory reaction that is toxic to sperm and eggs, thus works primarily by causing a chemical change that damages sperm and egg before they can meet.</li>
<li>May also make it difficult for the fertilized egg (ovum) to implant in the uterus.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-effective">How Effective?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-effective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="one-of-the-most-effective-and-long-lasting-methods">One of the most effective and long-lasting methods:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#one-of-the-most-effective-and-long-lasting-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Less than 1 pregnancy per 100 women using an IUD over the first year (6 to 8 per 1,000 women). This means that 992 to 994 of every 1,000 women using IUDs will not become pregnant.</p>
<p>A small risk of pregnancy remains beyond the first year of use and continues as long as the woman is using the IUD.</p>
<ul>
<li>Over 10 years of IUD use: About 2 pregnancies per 100 women</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="correcting-misunderstandings">Correcting Misunderstandings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#correcting-misunderstandings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

</li>
<li>
<p>Do not increase the risk of miscarriage when a woman becomes pregnant after the IUD is removed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Do not make women infertile.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Do not cause birth defects.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Do not cause cancer.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Do not move to the heart or brain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Do not cause discomfort or pain for the woman during sex.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Substantially reduce the risk of ectopic pregnancy.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>b) Levonorgestrel</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Intrauterine Device What Is the Levonorgestrel Intrauterine Device?</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The levonorgestrel intrauterine device (LNG-IUD) is a T-shaped plastic device that steadily releases small amounts of levonorgestrel each day. (Levonorgestrel is a progestin widely used in implants and oral contraceptive pills.)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-27d806a4.jpeg" alt="img-26.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>A specifically trained health care provider inserts it into a woman's uterus through her vagina and cervix. Also called the levonorgestrel-releasing intrauterine system, LNG-IUS, or Hormonal IUD.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Marketed under the brand name Mirena.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-it-works">How it works<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-it-works" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An IUCD coated with progestin works in a similar way as the copper coated one, but also works by;</p>
<ul>
<li>Works primarily by suppressing the growth of the lining of uterus (endometrium), thins the uterine lining.</li>
<li>Thickens the uterine mucus thus preventing sperm from meeting the egg.</li>
<li>Can also stops the release of egg form the ovary (ovulation) during the monthly period. This prevents the sperm from fertilizing the egg and implanting.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-effective">How Effective?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-effective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>One of the most effective and long-lasting methods:</li>
<li>Less than 1 pregnancy per 100 women using an LNG-IUD over the first year (2 per 1,000 women). This means that 998 of every 1,000 women using LNG-IUDs will not become pregnant.</li>
<li>A small risk of pregnancy remains beyond the first year of use and continues as long as the woman is using the LNG-IUD.</li>
<li>Over 5 years of LNG-IUD use: Less than 1 pregnancy per 100 women (5 to 8 per 1,000 women).</li>
<li>Approved for up to 5 years of use.</li>
<li>☑ Return of fertility after LNG-IUD is removed: No delay</li>
<li>☑ Protection against sexually transmitted infections (STIs): None</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side Effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Some users report the following:</li>
<li>Changes in bleeding patterns, including:</li>
<li>☑ Lighter bleeding and fewer days of bleeding</li>
<li>☑ Infrequent bleeding</li>
<li>☑ Irregular bleeding</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Rare:</li>
<li>Puncturing (perforation) of the wall of the uterus by the LNG-IUD or an instrument used for insertion. Usually heals without treatment.</li>
<li>Very rare:</li>
<li>Miscarriage, preterm birth, or infection in the very rare case that the woman becomes pregnant with the LNG-IUD in place.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="permanent-methods-of-family-planning">PERMANENT METHODS OF FAMILY PLANNING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#permanent-methods-of-family-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These are methods that are intended to provide lifelong, permanent and very effective protection against pregnancy. Reversal is usually impossible.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-female-sterilization">a) FEMALE STERILIZATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-female-sterilization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-is-female-sterilization">What Is Female Sterilization?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-female-sterilization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Permanent contraception for women who will not want more children.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The 2 surgical approaches most often used:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Minilaparotomy: This involves making a small incision in the abdomen. The fallopian tubes are brought to the incision to be cut or blocked.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Laparoscopy involves inserting a long thin tube with a lens in it into the abdomen through a small incision. This laparoscope enables the doctor to see and block or cut the fallopian tubes in the abdomen.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Also called tubal sterilization, tubal ligation, voluntary surgical contraception, tubectomy, bi-tubal ligation, tying the tubes, minilap, and “the operation.”</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Works because the fallopian tubes are blocked or cut. Eggs released from the ovaries cannot move down the tubes, and so they do not meet sperm.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-effective">How Effective?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-effective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>One of the most effective methods but carries a small risk of failure:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Less than 1 pregnancy per 100 women over the first year after having the sterilization procedure (5 per 1,000). This means that 995 of every 1,000 women relying on female sterilization will not become pregnant.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A small risk of pregnancy remains beyond the first year of use and until the woman reaches menopause.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Over 10 years of use:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ About 2 pregnancies per 100 women (18 to 19 per 1,000 women).</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Effectiveness varies slightly depending on how the tubes are blocked, but pregnancy rates are low with all techniques. One of the most effective techniques is cutting and tying the cut ends of the fallopian tubes after childbirth (postpartum tubal ligation).</p>
<ul>
<li>Fertility does not return because sterilization generally cannot be stopped or reversed. The procedure is intended to be permanent. Reversal surgery is difficult, expensive, and not available in most areas. When performed, reversal surgery often does not lead to pregnancy</li>
<li>Protection against sexually transmitted infections (STIs): None</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>None</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="known-health-benefits">Known health benefits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#known-health-benefits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Helps protect against:</p>
<ul>
<li>☑ Risks of pregnancy</li>
<li>☑ Pelvic inflammatory disease (PID)</li>
</ul>
<p>May help protect against:</p>
<ul>
<li>☑ Ovarian cancer</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="known-health-risk">Known health risk<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#known-health-risk" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Uncommon to extremely rare:</p>
<ul>
<li>☑ Complications of surgery and anesthesia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-of-surgery">Complications of Surgery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-surgery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Uncommon to extremely rare:</p>
<ul>
<li>☑ Female sterilization is a safe method of contraception. It requires surgery and anesthesia, however, which carry some risks such as infection or abscess of the wound. Serious complications are uncommon. Death, due to the procedure or anesthesia, is extremely rare.</li>
</ul>
<p>The risk of complications with local anesthesia is significantly lower</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>than with general anesthesia. Complications can be kept to a minimum if appropriate techniques are used and if the procedure is performed in an appropriate setting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="correcting-misunderstandings">Correcting Misunderstandings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#correcting-misunderstandings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Female sterilization:</li>
<li>Does not make women weak.</li>
<li>Does not cause lasting pain in back, uterus, or abdomen.</li>
<li>Does not remove a woman’s uterus or lead to a need to have it removed. Does not cause hormonal imbalances.</li>
<li>Does not cause heavier bleeding or irregular bleeding or otherwise change women’s menstrual cycles.</li>
<li>Does not cause any changes in weight, appetite, or appearance. Does not change women’s sexual behavior or sex drive.</li>
<li>Substantially reduces the risk of ectopic pregnancy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="who-can-have-female-sterilization-safe-for-all-women">Who Can Have Female Sterilization? Safe for All Women<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-can-have-female-sterilization-safe-for-all-women" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>With proper counseling and informed consent, any woman can have female sterilization safely, including women who:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Have no children or few children</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Are not married</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Do not have husband’s permission</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Are young</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Just gave birth (within the last 7 days)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Are breastfeeding</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Are infected with HIV, whether or not on antiretroviral therapy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In some of these situations, especially, careful counseling is important to make sure the woman will not regret her decision</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Women can have female sterilization:</p>
<ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-vasectomy">b) VASECTOMY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-vasectomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-is-vasectomy">What Is Vasectomy?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-vasectomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Permanent contraception for men who will not want more children.
Through a puncture or small incision in the scrotum, the provider locates each of the 2 tubes that carries sperm to the penis (vas deferens) and cuts or blocks it by cutting and tying it closed or by applying heat or electricity (cautery).
Also called male sterilization and male surgical contraception.
Works by closing off each vas deferens, keeping sperm out of semen.
Semen is ejaculated, but it cannot cause pregnancy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-effective">How Effective?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-effective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>One of the most effective methods but carries a small risk of failure:</p>
<ul>
<li>Where men cannot have their semen examined 3 months after the procedure to see if it still contains sperm, pregnancy rates are about 2 to 3 per 100 women over the first year after their partners have had a vasectomy. This means that 97 to 98 of every 100 women whose partners have had vasectomies will not become pregnant.</li>
<li>Where men can have their semen examined after vasectomy, less than 1 pregnancy per 100 women over the first year after their partners have had vasectomies (2 per 1,000). This means that 998 of every 1,000 women whose partners have had vasectomies will not become pregnant.</li>
<li>Vasectomy is not fully effective for 3 months after the procedure.</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Some pregnancies occur within the first year because the couple</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>does not use condoms or another effective method consistently and correctly in the first 3 months, before the vasectomy is fully effective.</p>
<p>A small risk of pregnancy remains beyond the first year after the vasectomy and until the man's partner reaches menopause.
✓ Over 3 years of use: About 4 pregnancies per 100 women</p>
<p>If the partner of a man who has had a vasectomy becomes pregnant, it may be because:
✓ The couple did not always use another method during the first 3 months after the procedure
✓ The provider made a mistake
✓ The cut ends of the vas deferens grew back together</p>
<p>Fertility does not return because vasectomy generally cannot be stopped or reversed. The procedure is intended to be permanent. Reversal surgery is difficult, expensive, and not available in most areas. When performed, reversal surgery often does not lead to pregnancy.
Protection against sexually transmitted infections (STIs): None</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects-known-health-risk-and-health-risk">Side effects, known health risk and health risk<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-known-health-risk-and-health-risk" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>None</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Uncommon to rare:
✓ Severe scrotal or testicular pain that lasts for months or years.</p>
<p>Uncommon to very rare:
✓ Infection at the incision site or inside the incision (uncommon with conventional incision technique; very rare with no-scalpel technique)</p>
<p>Rare:
✓ Bleeding under the skin that may cause swelling or bruising (hematoma).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="correcting-misunderstandings">Correcting Misunderstandings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#correcting-misunderstandings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<p>Vasectomy:</p>
<ul>
<li>Does not remove the testicles. In vasectomy the tubes carrying sperm from the testicles are blocked. The testicles remain in place.</li>
<li>Does not decrease sex drive.</li>
<li>Does not affect sexual function. A man's erection is as hard, it lasts as long, and he ejaculates the same as before.</li>
<li>Does not cause a man to grow fat or become weak, less masculine, or less productive.</li>
<li>Does not cause any diseases later in life.</li>
<li>Does not prevent transmission of sexually transmitted infections, including HIV.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="natural-family-planning-methods">NATURAL FAMILY PLANNING METHODS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#natural-family-planning-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-fertility-awareness-methods-what-are-fertility-awareness-methods">a) Fertility awareness methods What Are Fertility Awareness Methods?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-fertility-awareness-methods-what-are-fertility-awareness-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>“Fertility awareness” means that a woman knows how to tell when the fertile time of her menstrual cycle starts and ends. (The fertile time is when she can become pregnant.)</p>
<p>Sometimes called periodic abstinence or natural family planning.</p>
<p>A woman can use several ways, alone or in combination, to tell when her fertile time begins and ends.</p>
<p>Calendar-based methods involve keeping track of days of the menstrual cycle to identify the start and end of the fertile time. For example, Standard Days Method, which avoids unprotected vaginal sex on days 8 through 19 of the menstrual cycle, and calendar rhythm method.</p>
<p>Symptoms-based methods depend on observing signs of fertility.</p>
<ul>
<li>Cervical secretions: When a woman sees or feels cervical secretions, she may be fertile. She may feel just a little vaginal wetness.</li>
<li>Basal body temperature (BBT): A woman’s resting body temperature goes up slightly after the release of an egg (ovulation). She is not likely to become pregnant from 3 days after this temperature rise through the start of her next monthly bleeding. Her temperature stays higher until the beginning of her next monthly bleeding.</li>
<li>Examples: Two Day Method, BBT method, ovulation method (also known as Billing’s method or cervical mucus method), and symptothermal method.</li>
</ul>
<p>Work primarily by helping a woman know when she could become pregnant. The couple prevents pregnancy by avoiding unprotected</p>
<p>This document is available on
6
studocu
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>vaginal sex during these fertile days, usually by abstaining or by using condoms or a diaphragm. Some couples use spermicides or withdrawal, but these are among the least effective methods.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-effective">How Effective?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-effective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Effectiveness depends on the user: Risk of pregnancy is greatest when couples have sex on the fertile days without using another method.</li>
<li>As commonly used, in the first year about 15 pregnancies per 100 women using periodic abstinence. This means that 85 of every 100 women relying on periodic abstinence will not become pregnant.</li>
<li>Pregnancy rates with consistent and correct use vary for different types of fertility awareness methods.</li>
<li>In general, abstaining during fertile times is more effective than using another method during fertile times.</li>
<li>Return of fertility after fertility awareness methods are stopped: No delay</li>
<li>Protection against sexually transmitted infections (STIs): None</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="why-some-women-say-they-like-fertility-awareness-methods">Why some women say they like fertility awareness methods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-some-women-say-they-like-fertility-awareness-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Have no side effects</li>
<li>Do not require procedures and usually do not require supplies</li>
<li>Help women learn about their bodies and fertility</li>
<li>Allow some couples to adhere to their religious or cultural norms about contraception</li>
<li>Can be used to identify fertile days by both women who want to become pregnant and women who want to avoid pregnancy</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="explaining-how-to-use-calendar-based-methods">Explaining how to use Calendar-based Methods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#explaining-how-to-use-calendar-based-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="standard-days-method">Standard Days Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#standard-days-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

The couple avoids vaginal sex or uses condoms or a diaphragm during days 8 through 19. They can also use withdrawal or spermicides, but these are less effective.

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cycle-beads">Cycle beads<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cycle-beads" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A colour coded string of beads that indicates fertile and nonfertile days of a cycle.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-a63b86c4.jpeg" alt="img-27.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>Each bead represents a day of the menstrual cycle</li>
<li>On day 1: the first day of the monthly period. move the rubber ring to the red bead</li>
<li>The next day, move the ring to the next bead. Do this every day, even bleeding days.</li>
<li>White bead days are days when the woman can become pregnant. She should avoid unprotected sex.</li>
</ul>
<p>134</p>
<p>Brown bead days are days when pregnancy is unlikely and she can have unprotected sex.
If monthly bleeding begins again before reaching the dark brown bead, her menstrual cycle is shorter than 26 days.
If monthly bleeding does not begin before reaching the last brown bead, her menstrual cycle is longer than 32 days.</p>
<p>Calendar Rhythm Method</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Keep track of the days of the menstrual cycle</th><th>Before relying on this method, a woman records the number of days in each menstrual cycle for at least 6 months. The first day of monthly bleeding is always counted as day 1.</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Estimate the fertile time</td><td>The woman subtracts 18 from the length of her shortest recorded cycle. This tells her the estimated first day of her fertile time. Then she subtracts 11 days from the length of her longest recorded cycle. This tells her the estimated last day of her fertile time.</td></tr><tr><td>Avoid unprotected sex during fertile time</td><td>The couple avoids vaginal sex, or uses condoms or a diaphragm, during the fertile time. They can also use withdrawal or spermicides, but these are less effective.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>This document is available on
S
studocu
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>|  Update calculations monthly | She updates these calculations each month, always using the 6 most recent cycles.
Example:
If the shortest of her last 6 cycles was 27 days, 27-18 = 9. She starts avoiding unprotected sex on day 9.
If the longest of her last 6 cycles was 31 days, 31-11=20. She can have unprotected sex again on day 21.  |

<table><thead><tr><th></th><th>Thus, she must avoid unprotected sex from day 9 through day 20 of her cycle.</th></tr></thead></table>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="who-can-use-symptom-based-methods">Who can use symptom-based methods?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-can-use-symptom-based-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>All women can use symptoms-based methods. That is, no medical conditions prevent the use of these methods. However, some conditions can make them harder to use effectively.</p>
<ul>
<li>Caution means that additional or special counseling may be needed to ensure correct use of the method.</li>
<li>Delay means that use of a particular fertility awareness method should be delayed until the condition is evaluated or corrected. Give the client another method to use until she can start the symptoms-based method.</li>
<li>In the following situations, use caution with symptoms-based methods:</li>
<li>Recently had an abortion or miscarriage</li>
<li>Menstrual cycles have just started or have become less frequent or stopped due to older age. (Menstrual cycle irregularities are common in young women in the first</li>
</ul>
<p>137</p>
<p>several years after their first monthly bleeding and in older women who are approaching menopause. Identifying the fertile time may be difficult)</p>
<p>✓ A chronic condition that raises her body temperature (for basal body temperature and symptothermal methods)</p>
<p>In the following situations, <strong>delay</strong> starting symptoms-based methods:</p>
<p>✓ Recently gave birth or is breastfeeding. (<strong>Delay</strong> until normal secretions have returned—usually at least 6 months after childbirth for breastfeeding women and at least 4 weeks after childbirth for women who are not breastfeeding. For several months after regular cycles have returned, use with <strong>caution.</strong>)
✓ An acute condition that raises her body temperature (for basal body temperature and symptothermal methods)
✓ Irregular vaginal bleeding
✓ Abnormal vaginal discharge</p>
<p>In the following situation, <strong>delay</strong> or use <strong>caution</strong> with symptoms-based methods:</p>
<p>✓ Taking any drugs that change cervical secretions, for example, antihistamines, or drugs that raise body temperature, for example, antibiotics.</p>

<p>b) WITHDRAWL</p>
<p>L Withdrawal</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Just before ejaculation, the man withdraws his penis from his partner’s vagina and ejaculates outside the vagina, keeping his semen away from her external genitalia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Also known as coitus interruptus and “pulling out.”</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Works by keeping sperm out of the woman’s body.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>How Effective?</p>
<ul>
<li>Effectiveness depends on the user: Risk of pregnancy is greatest when the man does not withdraw his penis from the vagina before he ejaculates with every act of sex.</li>
<li>One of the least effective methods, as commonly used.</li>
<li>As commonly used, about 20 pregnancies per 100 women whose partners use withdrawal over the first year. This means that 80 of every 100 women whose partners use withdrawal will not become pregnant.</li>
</ul>

<p>When used correctly with every act of sex, about 4 pregnancies per 100 women whose partners use withdrawal over the first year.
Return of fertility after use of withdrawal is stopped: No delay
Protection against sexually transmitted infections: None</p>
<p>Side Effects, Health Benefits, and Health Risks</p>
<p>None</p>
<p>Who Can and Cannot Use Withdrawal?</p>
<p>All men can use withdrawal. No medical conditions prevent its use.
Withdrawal may be especially appropriate for couples who:</p>

have sex infrequently
have objections to using other method</p>

<p>Can be used at any time.
Effectiveness depends on the willingness and ability of the couple to use withdrawal with every act of intercourse.</p>

<p>c) LACTATION AMENORRHEA METHOD</p>
<p>What Is the Lactational Amenorrhea Method?</p>
<ul>
<li>A temporary family planning method based on the natural effect of breastfeeding on fertility. (“Lactational” means related to breastfeeding. “Amenorrhea” means not having monthly bleeding.)</li>
<li>The lactational amenorrhea method (LAM) requires 3 conditions and All the 3 must be met:</li>
<li>☑ The mother’s monthly bleeding has not returned.</li>
<li>☑ The baby is fully or nearly fully breastfed and is fed often, day and night.</li>
<li>☑ The baby is less than 6 months old.</li>
<li>“Fully breastfeeding” includes both exclusive breastfeeding (the infant receives no other liquid or food, not even water, in addition to breast milk) and almost-exclusive breastfeeding (the infant receives vitamins, water, juice, or other nutrients once in a while in addition to breast milk).</li>
<li>“Nearly fully breastfeeding” means that the infant receives some liquid or food in addition to breast milk, but the majority of feedings (more than three-fourths of all feeds) are breast milk.</li>
<li>Works primarily by preventing the release of eggs from the ovaries (ovulation). Frequent breastfeeding temporarily prevents the release of the natural hormones that cause ovulation.</li>
</ul>
<p>How Effective?</p>
<ul>
<li>Effectiveness depends on the user: Risk of pregnancy is greatest when a woman cannot fully or nearly fully breastfeed her infant.</li>
<li>As commonly used, about 2 pregnancies per 100 women using LAM in the first 6 months after childbirth. This means that 98 of every 100 women relying on LAM will not become pregnant.</li>
<li>When used correctly, less than 1 pregnancy per 100 women using LAM in the first 6 months after childbirth.</li>
<li>Return of fertility after LAM is stopped: Depends on how much the woman continues to breastfeed</li>
<li>Protection against sexually transmitted infections: None</li>
</ul>
<p>Side Effects</p>
<p>This document is available on
5
studocu
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>None. Any problems are the same as for other breastfeeding women.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="known-health-risk">Known Health Risk<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#known-health-risk" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="correcting-misunderstandings">Correcting Misunderstandings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#correcting-misunderstandings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The lactational amenorrhea method:</li>
<li>⚠️ Is highly effective when a woman meets all 3 LAM criteria. ⚠️ Is just as effective among fat or thin women.</li>
<li>⚠️ Can be used by women with normal nutrition. No special foods are required.</li>
<li>⚠️ Can be used for a full 6 months without the need for supplementary foods. Mother's milk alone can fully nourish a baby for the first 6 months of life. In fact, it is the ideal food for this time in a baby's life.</li>
<li>⚠️ Can be used for 6 months without worry that the woman will run out of milk. Milk will continue to be produced through 6 months and longer in response to the baby's suckling or the mother's expression of her milk.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="who-can-use-the-lactational-amenorrhea-method">Who Can Use the Lactational Amenorrhea Method?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-can-use-the-lactational-amenorrhea-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Medical Eligibility Criteria for the Lactation Amenorrhea Methods</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All breastfeeding women can safely use LAM, but a woman in the following circumstances may want to consider other contraceptive methods:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>✓ Has HIV infection
✓ Is using certain medications during breastfeeding (including mood-altering drugs, reserpine, ergotamine, anti-metabolites, cyclosporine, high doses of corticosteroids, bromocriptine, radioactive drugs, lithium, and certain anticoagulants)
✓ The newborn has a condition that makes it difficult to breastfeed (including being small-for-date or premature and needing intensive neonatal care, unable to digest food normally, or having deformities of the mouth, jaw, or palate)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lactation-amenorrhea-method-for-women-with-hiv">Lactation Amenorrhea Method for Women with HIV<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lactation-amenorrhea-method-for-women-with-hiv" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Women who are living with HIV can use LAM. Breastfeeding will not make their condition worse. However, there is a chance that mothers living with HIV, if they are not taking antiretroviral therapy (ART), will transmit HIV to their infants through breastfeeding.</li>
<li>Women taking ART can use LAM. Giving ART to an HIV-infected mother or an HIV- exposed infant very significantly reduces the risk of HIV transmission through breastfeeding. Among women who are not taking ART, 14% of their babies will be infected after 2 years of breastfeeding. Among women taking ART, less than 1% of their babies will be infected.</li>
<li>Exclusive breastfeeding reduces the risk of death from common childhood illness and improves the health and development of the child and also the health of the mother.</li>
<li>If national policy supports breastfeeding by women with HIV, they should receive the appropriate ART interventions and should exclusively breastfeed their infants for the first 6 months of life, introduce appropriate complementary foods at 6 months, and continue breastfeeding for the first 12 months. Breastfeeding should then stop only once a nutritionally adequate and safe diet without breast milk can be provided.</li>
<li>Urge women with HIV to use condoms along with LAM. Used consistently and correctly, condoms help prevent transmission of HIV and other STIs.</li>
</ul>

<p>At 6 months or earlier if her monthly bleeding has returned or she stops exclusive breastfeeding, a woman should begin to use another contraceptive method in place of LAM.</p>
<p>Why some say they like LAM</p>
<ul>
<li>It is a natural family planning method</li>
<li>It supports optimal breastfeeding, providing health benefits for the baby and the mother</li>
<li>It has no direct cost for family planning or for feeding the baby</li>
</ul>
<p>Explaining how to use LAM</p>
<p>|  Breastfeed often | An ideal pattern is feeding on demand (that is, whenever the baby wants to be fed) and at least 10 to 12 times a day in the first few weeks after childbirth and thereafter 8 to 10 times a day, including at least once at night in the first months.
Daytime feedings should be no more than 4 hours apart, and nighttime feedings no more than 6 hours apart.
Some babies may not want to breastfeed 8 to 10 times a day and may want to sleep through the night. These babies may need gentle encouragement to breastfeed more often.  |
| --- | --- |
|  Start other foods at 6 months | She should start giving other foods in addition to breast milk when the baby is 6 months old.  |</p>

<p>d) ABSTINEN</p>
<p>E What is</p>
<p>abstinence?</p>
<ul>
<li>Abstinence is simply not having sexual intercourse. If you're abstinent, it means you've decided not to have sex - this includes vaginal, oral and anal sex.</li>
<li>Abstinence prevents pregnancy by not giving the opportunity for semen to enter the vagina. A sperm can't fertilize an egg if you don't have intercourse</li>
</ul>
<p>How Effective?</p>
<ul>
<li>Effectiveness depends on the user: Abstinence is the only form of birth control that is 100% effective in preventing pregnancy</li>
<li>Practicing abstinence ensures that a woman Will not become pregnant because there is no opportunity for a sperm to fertilize an egg</li>
<li>Return of fertility after abstinence is stopped: Immediately.</li>
<li>Protection against sexually transmitted infections: Yes</li>
</ul>
<p>Advantages</p>
<p>154</p>
<p>It is free.
It is endorsed by many religious groups.
It is 100% effective in preventing pregnancy.
No medical or hormonal side effects.
It encourages you to build your relationship and express intimacy in other ways.
It does protect you from sexually transmitted infections, including HIV/AIDS, if there is no oral, anal or vaginal contact of any kind</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantage">Disadvantage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Both you and your partner must be committed to not having intercourse.</li>
<li>You might change your mind in the "heat of the moment," and not have alternative birth control on hand.</li>
<li>Pregnancy is still possible even without penetration if semen is on or near the vagina.</li>
<li>Other sexual activity such as oral sex can expose you to STIs</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="family-planning-counseling">FAMILY PLANNING COUNSELING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#family-planning-counseling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The main goal of family planning counseling is to improve the quality of life and reproductive health by empowering individuals and couples to excise their right to safe sexuality, and to decide whether and when to have children and how many to have. This goal is to provide opportunities for people, their circumstances, needs and options to help clients make informed decisions about contraception, fertility and sexual health.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>During counseling, the following should form the context of counseling;</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Bridge knowledge gap:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Provide brief information on the anatomy and physiology of reproductive health to clients</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explain about the contraceptive technology; that is, the benefits, risks, effectiveness and mode of actions (how the FP method works) for all available family planning methods</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Myths and beliefs should be told.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Help client make informed choice</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Consider that women may be unprepared to make their own choice. Encourage clients to take responsibility for decision-making</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Give complete information about the method chosen by the client.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Provide services</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Record should be kept for a client</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Give family planning services</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Should schedule follow-up</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The GATHER steps</p>
<ul>
<li>G - Greet clients in an open, respectful manner. Assure the client of confidentiality. Give as much time in listening than talking.</li>
<li>A - Ask clients about themselves. Help client talk about their family planning practices, intentions, concerns and wishes.</li>
<li>T - Tell client about choices. depending on the clients need, tell the client what reproductive health choices she/he might take. Focus on methods that interest the client. Also explain other services that the client may want</li>
<li>H - Help client makes an informed choice. Help the client think about options. Encourage the client to express opinions and ask questions. Consider medical eligibility for the family planning method that interest the client. In the end, make sure that the client has made clear decision.</li>
<li>E - Explain fully how to use the chosen method; after a client chooses a</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
S
studocu
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>family planning method, give her or him the supplies if appropriate. Encourage questions, and answer them openly and fully. Give condoms to any one at risk for sexually transmitted diseases (STDs) and encourage using condoms along with any other family planning method. Check that the clients understand how to use their methods.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)
158</p>
<p>R- Return visits should be welcomed: Discuss and agree when the client will return for follow-up or for more supplies if needed. Always invite the client to return any time for any reason.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="why-counseling-is-crucial-in-family-planning">Why Counseling is Crucial in Family Planning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-counseling-is-crucial-in-family-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Counseling help clients make and carry out their own choices about reproductive health and family planning</li>
<li>Counseling helps to make clients more satisfied with family planning methods</li>
<li>Counseling also helps to make clients to use family planning methods longer and more successfully.</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: Counseling should be tailored according to the need of each client. At the same time, most counseling about method choice should cover the following six topics;</p>
<ul>
<li>Effectiveness</li>
<li>Advantage and disadvantage</li>
<li>Side effects and complications</li>
<li>How to use</li>
<li>STI prevention</li>
<li>When to return</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tips-for-successful-counseling">Tips for Successful Counseling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tips-for-successful-counseling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Show every client respect, and help each client feel at ease.</li>
<li>Encourage the client to explain needs, express concerns, ask questions.</li>
<li>Let the client’s wishes and needs guide the discussion.</li>
<li>Be alert to related needs such as protection from sexually transmitted infections including HIV, and support for condom use.</li>
<li>Talk with the client in a private place, where no one else can hear.</li>
<li>Assure the client of confidentiality, that you will not tell others about your conversation or the client’s decisions.</li>
</ul>

<p>✓ Listen carefully. Listening is as important as giving correct information. Give just key information and instructions. Use words the client knows.
✓ Respect and support the client's informed decisions.
✓ Bring up side effects, if any, and take the client's concerns seriously.
✓ Check the client's understanding.
✓ Invite the client to come back any time for any reason.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reasons-for-not-using-contraceptives">Reasons for not using contraceptives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reasons-for-not-using-contraceptives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

✓ Religious and other opposition to family planning
✓ Fertility-related reasons, mainly desire for more children
✓ Opposition to use
✓ Lack of knowledge
✓ Method-related reason</p>

<p>UNIT 4: SEXUALLY TRANSMITTED INFECTIONS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this section, the learner should be able to;</p>
<ul>
<li>List the principal causes of sexually transmitted infections</li>
<li>Classifications of STIs</li>
<li>State the risk factors for STIs acquisition and transmission</li>

<li>Outline the public health significance of STIs</li>
<li>Understand STIs control strategies and obstacles.</li>
<li>Explain the effects of sexually transmitted infections</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Reproductive tract infections (RTIs) are infections of the genital tract of women and men. There are three types of RTIs:</p>
<p>a) Sexually transmitted infections (STIs)</p>
<p>Infections caused by viral, bacterial and parasitic microorganisms that are passed through sexual activity with an infected partner. however, other modes of transmission may include mother-to- child during pregnancy and childbirth, blood transfusion or other contact with blood and blood products. More than 40 have been identified, including Chlamydia, gonorrhea, hepatitis B and C, herpes, HPV, syphilis, trichomoniasis, and HIV.</p>
<p>b) Endogenous infections</p>
<p>Infections that result from an overgrowth of organisms normally present in the vagina. These infections are not usually sexually transmitted, and include bacterial vaginosis and candidiasis.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>S</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>c) Iatrogenic infections</p>
<p>Infections introduced into the reproductive tract by a medical procedure such as menstrual regulation, induced abortion, IUD insertion, or childbirth. This can happen if surgical instruments used in the procedure are not properly sterilized, or if an infection already present in the lower reproductive tract is pushed through the cervix into the upper reproductive tract.</p>
<p>These three types of RTIs overlap and should be considered together. For example, some STIs, like gonorrhea or Chlamydia, can be spread in the reproductive tract if not treated prior to a procedure. In addition, some non-sexual infections, such as candidiasis, can be passed on through sexual activity. Not all STIs are RTIs; and not all RTIs are sexually transmitted; STI refers to the way of transmission whereas RTI refers to the site where the infections develop.</p>
<p>PRINCIPLE CAUSES OF SEXUALLY TRANSMITTED INFECTIONS</p>
<p>Chlamydia</p>
<p>The organism Chlamydia trachomatis causes inflammation of the female cervix. Infection may ascend through the reproductive tract and cause pelvic inflammatory disease.</p>
<p>In the male, it may cause urethritis, which may also ascend and lead to epididymitis. Chlamydia infection is often present in conjunction with other sexually transmitted diseases. The same organism causes trachoma, an eye infection that is the primary cause of blindness worldwide.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>This document is available on
S
studocu
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="gonorrhea">Gonorrhea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gonorrhea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is caused by <em>Neisseria gonorrhoeae</em>, which infects the mucosa of the reproductive and urinary tracts. In the male, suppurative urethritis occurs and the infection may spread to the prostate gland, epididymis and testes. In the female the infection may spread from vulvar glands, vagina and cervix to the body of the uterus, uterine tubes, ovaries and peritoneum. Healing by fibrosis in the female may cause obstruction of the uterine tubes, leading to infertility. In the male it may cause urethral stricture.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="syphilis">Syphilis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#syphilis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This disease is caused by <em>Treponema pallidum</em>. There are three clearly marked stages. After an incubation period of several weeks, the primary sore (chancre) appears at the site of infection, e.g., the vulva, vagina, perineum, penis or round the mouth. In the female the primary sore may be undetected if it is internal. After several weeks, the chancre subsides spontaneously. The secondary stage, 3 to 4 months after infection, involves systemic symptoms including lymphadenopathy, skin rashes and mucosal ulceration of the mouth and genital tract. There may then be a latent period of between 3 and 10 years. Tertiary lesions (gummas) then develop in many organs, including skin, bone and mucous membranes, and may involve the nervous system, leading to general paralysis and dementia.</p>
<p>Sexual transmission occurs during the primary and secondary stages when discharge from lesions is highly infectious. Congenital transmission from mother to fetus carries a high risk of stillbirth.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="trichomonas-vaginalis">Trichomonas vaginalis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#trichomonas-vaginalis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These protozoa cause acute vulvovaginitis with irritating, offensive discharge. It is usually sexually transmitted and is commonly present in women with gonorrhoea. Males are often asymptomatic.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="candidiasis">Candidiasis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#candidiasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>163</p>
<p>The yeast Candida albicans is frequently a commensal in the normal vagina and causes no problems. It is normally prevented from flourishing by vaginal acidity, but in certain circumstances it proliferates, causing candidiasis (thrush).</p>
<p>Common precipitating factors include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Antibiotic therapy, which kills the bacteria that keep vaginal pH low (Lactobacteria)</li>
<li>Pregnancy</li>
<li>Reduced immune function</li>
<li>Diabetes mellitus.</li>
</ul>
<p>In women, persistent itch is the main symptom, with discharge, swelling and erythema of the vulvar area.</p>
<p>Acquired immune deficiency syndrome (AIDS) and hepatitis B infection</p>
<p>These viral conditions may be sexually transmitted, but there are no local signs of infection. For a description of AIDS and HIV and hepatitis B.</p>
<p>A. Non-specific genital infection</p>
<p>This is increasingly common, especially in males. General symptoms include painful urination and urethral discharge, and there is a wide range of possible causative organisms. Some cases are not sexually transmitted and arise from, for example, urinary tract infection or the presence of a foreign body in the urethra.</p>
<p>Genital herpes</p>
<p>One form of the herpes virus, Herpes simplex 2 (HSV2) is associated with genital infections. Initial infection tends to present as clusters of small, painful ulcers on the external genitalia. There is often fever and headache. Recurrences of the disease occur because the virus establishes itself within the dorsal root ganglion, from where it can be reactivated from time to time.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification-of-stis">Classification of STIs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-stis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
