<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risk-factors-for-stis-acquisitions-and-transmission">Risk factors for STIs Acquisitions and Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors-for-stis-acquisitions-and-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Participation in unprotected vaginal, oral or anal sex (no condom or dental dam used)</li>
<li>Genital to genital sexual contact</li>
<li>Previous history of STIs.</li>
<li>Having multiple sexual partners</li>
<li>Use of non-barrier contraceptives, such as spermicides especially those containing n-9 due to disruption of the genital epithelium</li>
<li>Use of injection drugs, alcohol or other substances that can impair decision making ability</li>
<li>Use of PrEP (Pre-exposure prophylaxis) which may lead to decreased use of condoms hence increased risk</li>
<li>Inconsistent and irregular use of condoms during sex</li>
<li>Vaginal practices e.g., Douching</li>
<li>IUD placement for women especially within the first 20 days of placement</li>
<li>Use of spermicides</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-stis">Treatment of STIs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-stis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="syndromic-approach-to-sti-management">Syndromic Approach to STI Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#syndromic-approach-to-sti-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The syndromic approach to STI management uses flowcharts to guide diagnosis and treatment of Sexually transmitted infections.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A syndrome is a combination of symptoms and signs that appear together and characterize a disease or medical condition (e.g., a combination of pain on passing urine and urethral discharge).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Many common STIs present with similar signs and symptoms and can therefore be grouped into a small number of syndromes. The aim of the syndromic approach to STI management is to identify each syndrome and treat it with a combination of antimicrobial agents effective against the main causal pathogens.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Flow charts used for syndromic management of STIs are graphic representations of logical sequences for decision-making towards the management of clients who present symptoms of STIs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It presents a series of consecutive decisions and actions that need to be taken, starting with specific symptoms and signs, through identification of syndromes and finally the choice of treatment.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="advantages-of-syndromic-approach-to-sti-management">Advantages of Syndromic Approach to STI Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-syndromic-approach-to-sti-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The advantages of the syndromic approach to STI management are:</li>
<li>The flow charts used in this approach represent a combination of simple, practical scientific information for decision making in primary health settings and in most cases does not require highly trained health care providers.</li>
<li>STI managed is based on characteristic symptoms and signs without using expensive lab equipment.</li>
<li>It allows for prompt initiation of STI treatment at first contact with clients reducing delays in diagnosis.</li>
<li>The treatment covers the entire range of known causative agents for the syndrome, reducing chances of treatment failure and expediting effective treatment which reduces the risk of transmission and development of serious complications.</li>
<li>The use of flow charts in this approach standardizes STI treatment across diverse settings and allows for comparative results across sites, builds client confidence, and allows for efficient centralized procurement of drugs.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>S</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>○ It allows for rapid, effective management of STIs in busy primary health care clinics.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages-of-syndromic-approach-to-sti-management">Disadvantages of Syndromic approach to STI management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages-of-syndromic-approach-to-sti-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Syndromic approach to STI management however has one major disadvantage.</li>
<li>Many patients may receive more drugs than they need hence resulting in their being over treated</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: Despite its disadvantages, the syndromic approach to STI management can lead to substantial improvements in quality and effectiveness of STI case management and control. It is recommended that this approach be utilized as the main approach for management of STIs in Kenya. In extreme cases of treatment failure, patients should be referred to the designated referral health facilities equipped to manage STIs etiologically.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="public-health-significance-of-stis">Public Health Significance of STIs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#public-health-significance-of-stis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-of-stis-to-the-public">Effects of STIS to the public<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-stis-to-the-public" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The links between STIs and HIV is one of the reasons that force the world to give attention to almost neglected sexually transmitted infections, because:</p>
<ul>
<li>The presence of an untreated STI enhances both acquisition and transmission of HIV. HSV-2 plays an important role in the transmission of HIV infection.</li>
<li>STI treatment is an important HIV prevention strategy in a general population</li>
<li>Integration of HIV/AIDS programs with STIs prevention and care programs is economically advantageous (similar interventions and target audiences). NASCOP in Kenya.</li>
<li>Clinical services offering STI care are important for providing information and education about STIs including HIV in order to promote lower risk behavior.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Another reason to consider STIs as public health problems is because STIs can lead to the development of serious complications like:</p>
<ul>
<li>In women: STIs can lead to cervical cancer, pelvic inflammatory disease, chronic pelvic pain, ectopic pregnancy and infertility. That is, untreated gonococcal and chlamydial infections in women will result in pelvic inflammatory disease in up to 40% of cases. One in four of these will result in infertility.</li>
<li>In men: STIs can lead to sub-fertility.</li>
<li>In newborn: Mother-to-child transmission of STI can result in stillbirth, neonatal death, low-birth weight babies, prematurity, sepsis, pneumonia, neonatal conjunctivitis and congenital deformities.</li>
<li>Syphilis can result in congenital syphilis for the baby and fatal cardiac, neurological and other complications in adults</li>
<li>Genital warts can lead to ano-genital cancers</li>
<li>In pregnancy, untreated early syphilis will result in a stillbirth, thus contributing to neonatal deaths, premature births or low birth weights babies.</li>
<li>The socioeconomic costs of STIs and their complications are substantial:</li>
<li>Ranks among the top 10 reasons for health-care visits in most developing countries, and substantially drain both national health budgets and household income.</li>
<li>Care for the sequel of STIs accounts for a large proportion of tertiary health-care costs</li>
<li>Social costs of STIs include conflict between sexual partners and domestic violence.</li>
</ul>
<p>These are the main reasons to consider STIs as public health problems and to design and implement appropriate intervention both preventive and curative.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sti-control-strategies">STI Control Strategies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sti-control-strategies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Abstinence</li>
<li>Prevention by promoting safer sexual behaviors;</li>
<li>What is safer sex? It is any sexual activity that reduces the risk of passing STI and HIV from one person to another.</li>
<li>Some safer sex practices:</li>
<li>Consistent use of condom every time individual is having sex</li>
<li>Reducing the number of sex partners. Sex with uninfected monogamous is safe</li>
<li>Massaging, rubbing touching, dry kissing, hugging or masturbation instead of intercourse</li>
<li>To be away from unsafe sexual practices, like “dry sex”</li>
<li>Not to have intercourse with partner having genital sore or discharge</li>
<li>General access to quality condoms at affordable prices; to help increase their use, and reduce barriers to utilization.</li>
<li>Promotion of early recourse to health services by people suffering from STIs and by their partners;</li>
<li>Inclusion of STI treatment in basic health services;</li>
<li>Specific services for populations with frequent or unplanned high-risk sexual behaviors</li>
</ul>

<li>Screening of clinically asymptomatic patients;</li>

<p>Prevention and care of congenital syphilis and neonatal conjunctivitis;
Behavioral change interventions with explicit messages about the risks of STIs.
Human Papilloma Vaccine (HPV) for females aged 11-12 years.
Vaccination against Hepatitis A and B for all men sexing men (MSM) is recommended.
Involvement of all relevant stakeholders, including the private sector and the community, in prevention of STIs and prompt contact with health services for those requiring care. Thus, any effective control strategy requires identification of vulnerable populations and working towards mitigation strategies with them. An individual is vulnerable to STIs when his/her ability to avoid infection is diminished by inadequate personal knowledge or skills, cultural norms or circumstances. These vulnerabilities include:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-that-increase-vulnerability-to-stis">Factors that increase vulnerability to STIs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-that-increase-vulnerability-to-stis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<p>NOTE:</p>
<p>Many people with an STI/RTI do not seek treatment since they are asymptomatic or have mild symptoms and do not realize that anything is wrong. Others who have symptoms may prefer to treat themselves or seek treatment at pharmacies or from traditional healers. Even those who come to a clinic may not be properly diagnosed and treated. In the end, only a small proportion of people with an STI/RTI may be cured and avoid re-infection.</p>
<p>In order to address these challenges, health providers should:</p>
<ul>
<li>Raise awareness in the community about STIs/RTIs and how they can be prevented</li>
<li>Promote early use of clinic services.</li>
<li>Promote safer sexual practices when counseling clients.</li>
<li>Detect infections that are not obvious.</li>
<li>Prevent iatrogenic infection</li>
<li>Manage symptomatic STI/RTI effectively</li>
<li>Counsel patients on staying uninfected after treatment.</li>
</ul>
<p>Obstacles to Provision of Services for STI Control</p>
<ul>
<li>Decline in interest and resources for STIs prevention and control globally in favor of ART and VCT</li>
<li>Lack of integration of prevention and care activities for STIs (including HIV) into sexual and reproductive health services</li>
<li>Problem with Syndromic management of women with vaginal discharge, especially in low prevalence areas</li>
<li>Intervention efforts to prevent STIs have failed to take into consideration the full range of the underlying determinants.</li>
<li>Inability to ensure consistent supplies of STI medicines and condoms</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>Counseling on risk reduction is also usually lacking</li>
<li>Inadequate participation of partners, especially communities</li>
<li>Diagnostic problem: either asymptomatic or do not seek care</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pelvic-inflammatory-disease-pid">Pelvic inflammatory disease (PID)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pelvic-inflammatory-disease-pid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This condition is usually a consequence of sexually transmitted infections (STIs). It usually begins as vulvovaginitis and may spread upwards to the cervix, uterus, uterine tubes and ovaries.</li>
<li>Upward spread can also occur when infection is present in the vagina before a surgical procedure, childbirth or miscarriage, especially if some of the products of conception are retained.</li>
</ul>

Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Complications of PID include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Infertility due to obstruction of uterine tubes</li>
<li>Peritonitis</li>
<li>Intestinal obstruction due to adhesions between the bowel and the uterus and/or uterine tubes</li>
<li>Bacteremia, which may lead to meningitis, endocarditis or suppurative arthritis.</li>
</ul>
<p>Vulvar disorders</p>
<p>a) Atrophic dystrophy</p>
<p>Vaginal atrophy</p>
<ul>
<li>Caused by progressive muscle weakness and shrinkage (atrophy)... the muscle fibres degenerate over time due to genetic changes affecting the proteins leading to muscle mass and strength loss.</li>
<li>This is thinning of vulvar epithelium and the formation of fibrous tissue, occurring after the menopause due to oestrogen withdrawal.</li>
<li>It predisposes to infection, especially in debilitated women, and to malignant epithelial neoplasia.</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Vulvar intraepithelial neoplasia (VIN)</p>
<ul>
<li>This refers to early neoplastic (cancerous) changes in epithelial cells of the vulva.</li>
<li>It is commonest in younger women, often those infected with human papilloma virus, and may proceed to malignancy.</li>
</ul>
<p>Imperforate hymen</p>
<ul>
<li>This congenital abnormality may not be noticed until the onset of menstruation.</li>
<li>When complete (imperforate), the hymen forms a barrier in the vagina. Blood accumulates in the vagina, uterus and uterine tubes with each menstrual cycle, and it may enter the peritoneal cavity and cause peritonitis.</li>
<li>The uterine tubes may become obstructed by coagulated blood, leading to infertility.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Disorders of the cervix</p>
<p>Cervical carcinoma</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Dysplastic changes, referred to as cervical intraepithelial neoplasia (CIN) begin in the deepest layer of cervical epithelium, usually at the junction of the stratified squamous epithelium of the lower third of the cervical canal with the secretory epithelium of the upper two-thirds.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dysplasia may progress to involve the full thickness of epithelium.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Not all dysplasia develops into malignant disease, but it is not possible to predict how far development will go, and whether it will remain static or regress.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Early detection with a screening programme can allow abnormal tissue to be removed before it becomes malignant.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Established malignancy is staged according to how extensive the tumor is.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stage I refers to disease confined to the cervix. Stages II through IV reflect increasing spread, including involvement of the rectum, bladder and structures out with the pelvis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Early spread is via lymph nodes and local spread is commonly to the uterus, vagina, bladder and rectum.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In the late stages, spread via the blood to the liver, lungs and bones may occur.</p>
</li>
</ul>

<li>The disease takes 15 to 20 years to develop and it occurs mostly between 35 and 50 years of age.</li>
<li>It is likely that a significant proportion of cases are due to the transmission of some sexually transmitted carcinogen.</li>
<li>Risk factors include having frequent sexual intercourse with multiple partners from an early age, all of which increase the likelihood of being exposed to a carcinogenic agent.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disorders-of-the-uterine-body">Disorders of the uterine body<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disorders-of-the-uterine-body" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-endometritis">a. Endometritis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-endometritis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>This is usually caused by non-specific infection, following childbirth or miscarriage, especially if fragments of membranes or placenta have been retained in the uterus.</li>
<li>It may also be caused by an intrauterine contraceptive device (IUD). The inflammation may subside after removal of retained products or the IUD.</li>
<li>The infection may spread to surrounding pelvic structures, e.g., uterine tubes, or deeper layers of the uterus.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="b-endometriosis">b. Endometriosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-endometriosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>This is the growth of endometrial tissue outside the uterus, usually in the ovaries, uterine tubes and other pelvic structures.</li>
<li>The ectopic tissue, like the uterine endometrium, responds to fluctuations in sex hormone levels during the menstrual cycle, causing menstrual-type bleeding into the lower abdomen and, in the ovaries, the formation of coloured cysts, 'chocolate cysts.</li>
<li>There is intermittent pain due to swelling, and recurrent haemorrhage causes fibrous tissue formation.</li>
<li>Ovarian endometriosis may lead to pelvic inflammation, infertility and extensive pelvic adhesions, involving the ovaries, uterus, uterine ligaments and the bowel.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="c-adenomyosis">c. Adenomyosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-adenomyosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>This is the growth of endometrium within the myometrium. The ectopic tissue may cause general or localized uterine enlargement. The lesions</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>may cause dysmenorrhea and irregular excessive bleeding (menorrhagia), usually beginning between 40 and 50 years of age.</p>
<p>This document is available on
© studocu
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>d. Endometrial hyperplasia</p>
<ul>
<li>Hyperplasia of the endometrium is associated with high blood oestrogen levels, e.g., in obesity, oestrogen therapy or an ovarian tumour.</li>
<li>Sometimes it is associated with increased risk of malignant change.</li>
</ul>
<p>e. Leiomyoma (fibroid, myoma)</p>
<ul>
<li>These are very common, often multiple, benign tumours of myometrium.</li>
<li>They are firm masses of smooth muscle encapsulated in compressed muscle fibres and they vary greatly in size.</li>
<li>Large tumours may undergo degenerative changes if they outgrow their blood supply, leading to necrosis, fibrosis and calcification.</li>
<li>They develop during the reproductive period and may be hormone dependent, enlarging during pregnancy and when oral contraceptives are used.</li>
<li>They tend to regress after the menopause.</li>
<li>Large tumours may cause pelvic discomfort, frequency of micturition, menorrhagia, irregular bleeding, dysmenorrhea and reduced fertility. Malignant change is rare.</li>
</ul>
<p>f. Endometrial carcinoma</p>
<ul>
<li>This occurs mainly in women who have never been pregnant and is most common between 50 and 60 years of age.</li>
<li>The incidence is increased when an oestrogen-secreting tumour is present and in women who are obese, hypertensive or diabetic, because they tend to have a high level of blood oestrogen.</li>
<li>As the tumour grows, there is often ulceration and vaginal bleeding.</li>
<li>Endometrium has no lymphatics, so lymph spread is delayed until there is extensive local spread that involves other pelvic structures.</li>
<li>Distant metastases, spread in blood or lymph, develop later, most commonly in the liver, lungs and bones. Invasion of the ureters leads to hydronephrosis and uremia, commonly the cause of death.</li>
</ul>

<p>Disorders of the uterine tubes and ovaries</p>
<p>a. Acute salpingitis</p>
<ul>
<li>Salpingitis is <strong>inflammation of the uterine tubes</strong>. It is usually due to infection spreading from the uterus, and only occasionally from the peritoneal cavity.</li>
<li>The uterine tubes may be left permanent</li>
</ul>

<p>damaged by fibrous scar tissue, which can cause obstruction and infertility.</p>
<ul>
<li>Infection may spread into the peritoneum and involve the ovaries.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-ectopic-pregnancy">b. Ectopic pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-ectopic-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This is the implantation of a fertilized ovum outside the uterus, most commonly in a uterine tube. As the fetus grows the tube may rupture and its contents enter the peritoneal cavity, causing acute inflammation (peritonitis) and possibly severe intraperitoneal haemorrhage (bleeding).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-ovarian-tumours">c. Ovarian tumours<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-ovarian-tumours" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The majority of ovarian tumours are benign, usually occurring between 20 and 45 years of age.</li>
<li>The rest occur mostly between 45 and 65 years and are divided between borderline malignancy (low-grade cancer) and frank malignancy.</li>
<li>Ovarian cancer is associated with developed societies, higher socioeconomic groups, and, in some families, a genetic susceptibility.</li>
<li>Pregnancy and the use of the contraceptive pill have a protective effect.</li>
<li>Most malignancies of the ovary arise from epithelium, but some arise from the germ cells of the ovary, or from stromal cells.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="d-metastatic-ovarian-tumour">d. Metastatic ovarian tumour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-metastatic-ovarian-tumour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The ovaries are a common site of metastatic spread from primary tumours in other pelvic organs, the breast, stomach, pancreas and biliary tract.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disorders-of-the-breast">Disorders of the breast<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disorders-of-the-breast" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Mastitis (inflammation of the breast)</p>
<ul>
<li>Acute non-suppurative mastitis</li>
<li>This occurs during lactation and is associated with painful congestion and oedema of the breast. It is of hormonal origin.</li>
<li>Acute suppurative (pyogenic) mastitis</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>The microbes enter through a nipple abrasion caused by the infant sucking. The most common causative microbes are <strong>Staphylococcus aureus</strong> and <strong>Streptococcus pyogenes</strong> usually acquired by the infant while in hospital. The infection spreads along the mammary ducts of a lobe causing localized swelling and redness. If it does not resolve it can become chronic and an abscess may form.</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Tumours of the breast</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>Benign tumours</strong> - fibroadenoma, breast cysts, fibrocystic changes, adenosis, papilloma, lipoma, phyllodes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Most breast tumours (90%) are benign.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Fibroadenomas</strong> are the commonest type and occur <strong>any time after puberty</strong>; incidence peaks in the third decade.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Some are cystic and some solid, and they usually occur in women nearing the menopause.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They may originate from secretory cells, fibrous tissue or from ducts.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Malignant tumours</strong></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The most common types of tumour are usually painless lumps found in the upper outer quadrant of the breast.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There is considerable fibrosis around the tumour that may cause <strong>retraction of the nipple and necrosis and ulceration of the overlying skin</strong>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is increasingly common between 35 and 70 years.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Early spread beyond the breast is via lymph to the axillary and internal mammary nodes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Local invasion involves the <strong>pectoral muscles and the pleura</strong>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Blood-spread metastases may occur later in many organs and bones, especially lumbar and thoracic vertebrae.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The causes of breast cancer are not known, but an important predisposing factor appears to be high oestrogen exposure.</p>
</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="penile-and-urethral-infections">Penile and Urethral infections<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#penile-and-urethral-infections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="infections-of-the-penis">Infections of the penis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#infections-of-the-penis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Inflammation of the glans and prepuce may be caused by a specific or non-specific infection.</li>
<li>In non-specific infections, or balanitis, lack of personal hygiene is an important predisposing factor, especially if phimosis is present, i.e., the orifice in the foreskin (prepuce) is too small to allow for its normal retraction.</li>
<li>If the infection becomes chronic there may be fibrosis of the foreskin, which increases the phimosis.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="infections-of-the-urethra">Infections of the urethra<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#infections-of-the-urethra" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Gonococcal urethritis is the most common specific infection.</li>
<li>Non-specific infection may be spread from the bladder (cystitis) or be introduced during catheterisation, cystoscopy or surgery.</li>
<li>Both types may spread throughout the system to the prostate, seminal vesicles, epididymis and testes.</li>

<p>Epididymis and testes
a) Infections</p>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)
185</p>
<ul>
<li>Non-specific epididymitis and orchitis are usually due to spread of infection from the urethra, commonly following prostatectomy.</li>
<li>The microbes may spread either through the deferent duct (vas deferens) or via lymph.</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Specific epididymitis</p>
<ul>
<li>This is usually caused by gonorrhoea spread from the urethra.</li>
</ul>
<p>c) Orchitis (inflammation of the testis)</p>
<ul>
<li>This is commonly caused by mumps virus, blood-borne from the parotid glands.</li>
<li>Acute inflammation with oedema occurs about 1 week after the appearance of parotid swelling.</li>
<li>The infection is usually unilateral but, if bilateral, severe damage to germinal epithelium of the seminiferous tubules may result in sterility.</li>
</ul>
<p>d) Undescended testis (cryptorchidism)</p>
<ul>
<li>During embryonic life the testes develop within the abdominal cavity, but descend into the scrotum prior to birth.</li>
<li>If they fail to do this and the condition is not corrected, infertility is likely to follow and the risk of testicular cancer is increased.</li>
</ul>
<p>e) Hydrocele</p>
<ul>
<li>This is the most common form of scrotal swelling and is accumulation of serous fluid in the tunica vaginalis.</li>
<li>The onset may be acute and painful or chronic.</li>
<li>It may be congenital or be secondary to another disorder of the testis or epididymis.</li>
</ul>
<p>f) Testicular tumors</p>
<p>Most testicular tumors are malignant, the commonest malignancies in young men.</p>
<p>They occur in childhood and early adulthood when the affected testis has not descended or has been late in descending into the scrotum.</p>
<p>The tumor tends to remain localized for a considerable time but eventually spreads in lymph to pelvic and abdominal lymph nodes, and more widely in the blood.</p>
<p>Occasionally, hormone-secreting tumors develop and may cause precocious development in boys.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prostate-gland">Prostate gland<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prostate-gland" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) Infections</p>
<p>Acute prostatitis is usually caused by non-specific infection, spread from the urethra or bladder, often following catheterization, cystoscopy, urethral dilation or prostate surgery. Chronic infection may follow an acute attack. Fibrosis of the gland may occur during healing, causing urethral stricture or obstruction.</p>
<p>b) Benign prostatic enlargement</p>
<p>Hyperplastic nodules form around the urethra and may obstruct the flow of urine, causing urinary retention. Urethral stricture may prevent the bladder emptying completely during micturition, predisposing to infection, which may spread upwards, causing pyelonephritis and other complications. Prostatic enlargement is common in men over 50, affecting up to 70% of men aged over 70. The cause is not clear, but it may be an acceleration of the ageing process associated with the decline in androgen secretion, which changes the androgen/oestrogen balance.</p>
<p>c) Malignant prostatic tumours</p>
<p>These are a relatively common cause of death in men over 50. The carcinogen is not known but changes in the androgen/oestrogen balance may be significant or viruses may be involved. Invasion of local tissues is widespread before lymph-spread metastases develop in pelvic and abdominal lymph nodes. Blood-spread metastases in bone are common and bone formation rather than bone destruction is a common feature. Lumbar vertebrae are common sites, possibly due to retrograde spread along the walls of veins. Bone metastases are often the first indication of malignant prostatic tumours.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="breast">Breast<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#breast" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Breast tissue in men consists of ducts and stroma only.</p>
<p>a. Gynecomastia]</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>

<p>This is proliferation of breast tissue in men.</p>
<p>It usually affects only one breast and is benign.</p>
<p>It is common in adolescents and older men, and is often associated with:</p>
<ul>
<li>Endocrine disorders, especially those associated with high oestrogen levels</li>
<li>Cirrhosis of the liver</li>

<p>b. Malignant tumours</p>
<p>These develop in a small number of men, usually in the older age groups.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sexual-health">SEXUAL HEALTH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexual-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Sexual health is a state of physical, emotional, mental and social well-being related to sexuality; it is not merely the absence of disease, dysfunction or infirmity.</p>
<p>Sexual health requires a positive and respectful approach to sexuality and sexual relationships, as well as the possibility of having pleasurable and safe sexual experiences, free of coercion, discrimination and violence. For sexual health to be attained and maintained, the sexual rights of all persons must be respected, protected and fulfilled</p>
<p>Sexual health is the ability to embrace and enjoy our sexuality throughout our lives. It is an important part of our physical and emotional health. Being sexually healthy means:</p>
<ul>
<li>Understanding that sexuality is a natural part of life and involves more than sexual behavior.</li>
<li>Recognizing and respecting the sexual rights we all share.</li>
<li>Having access to sexual health information, education, and care.</li>
<li>Making an effort to prevent unintended pregnancies and STDs and seek care and treatment when needed.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>○ Being able to experience sexual pleasure, satisfaction, and intimacy when desired.
○ Being able to communicate about sexualhealth with others including sexual partners and healthcare providers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="safe-sexual-health-practices">Safe Sexual health practices<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#safe-sexual-health-practices" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Using barrier methods can lower the risk of contracting STIs. These methods can include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Using external or internal condoms for penetrative intercourse, including with sex toys</li>
<li>Using condoms or dental dams for oral sex</li>
<li>Using gloves for manual stimulation or penetration</li>
</ul>
<p>♦ Maintaining good hygiene before and after sexual contact can also help prevent STI transmission. This can include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Washing your hands before any sexual contact</li>
<li>Rinsing off after sexual contact</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sexual-dysfunction">Sexual dysfunction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexual-dysfunction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It refers to a problem that can happen during any phase of sexual response cycle that prevent individual or couple from experiencing satisfaction from sexual activity.</p>
<p>The sexual response cycle traditionally includes excitement, plateau, organism and resolution. Desire and arousal are both part of excitement phase of the sexual response. It is important to know that women do not always go through these phases in order.</p>

<p>Types of Sexual Dysfunction</p>
<p>Dysfunction in male:</p>
<ul>
<li>Erectile dysfunction: inability to achieve or maintain an erection (hard penis) suitable for intercourse.</li>
<li>Premature ejaculation: inability to control timing of an erection.</li>
<li>Retarded ejaculation: absent or delayed ejaculation despite enough sexual stimulation</li>
<li>Inhibited sexual desire</li>
</ul>
<p>Dysfunction of female</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Primary orgasmic dysfunction: inability to achieve organisms.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Secondary orgasmic dysfunction: inability to reach organism both one has had one before.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vaginismus: inability to relax the vaginal muscle enough to allow intercourse.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diminished lubrication: inadequate vaginal lubrication before and during intercourse.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dyspareunia: painful sexual intercourse.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>In both men and women</strong></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Desire disorder: lack of sexual desire or interest in sex.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Arousal disorder: inability to become physically aroused or excited during sexual activity. Organism disorder: delay or absence of organism (climax)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pain disorder: pain during intercourse.</p>
</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Traditional</p>
<p>Practices</p>
<p>Tradition represents the sum total of all behaviours that are learned, shared by a group of people and transmitted from generation to generation. Thus, traditional cultural practices reflect values and beliefs held by members of community for periods often spanning generations. Every social grouping in the entire world has specific traditional cultural practices and beliefs, some of which are beneficial to all members, while others are harmful to a specific group, such as women.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="harmful-practices">Harmful practices<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#harmful-practices" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Some of these harmful practices include;</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Female genital mutilation (FGM):
Female genital mutilation (FGM), or female circumcision as it is sometimes erroneously referred to, involves surgical removal of parts or all of the most sensitive female genital organs. It is an age-old practice which is perpetuated in many communities around the world simply because it is customary. FGM forms an important part of the rites of passage ceremony for some communities, marking the coming of age of the female child. It is
believed that, by mutilating the female's genital organs, her sexuality will be controlled; but above all it is to ensure a woman's virginity before marriage and chastity thereafter. In fact, FGM imposes on women and the girl child a catalogue of health complications and untold psychological problems. The practice of FGM violates, among other international human rights laws, the right of the child to the "enjoyment of the highest attainable standard of reproductive health.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Severely restricted weight gain during pregnancy. That is, nutritional taboos
Food taboos are common practices of certain food items for pregnant and/or lactating women or girls in general. Cultural practices, including nutritional taboos, ensure that pregnant women are deprived of essential nutriments, and as a result they tend to suffer from iron and protein deficiencies. this is because foods that are good sources of energy and protein are not allowed to be consumed by pregnant women for reasons such as difficult and prolonged labor due to fears of a large baby</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Forced feeding of women
This involves forcing the young girls and women to feed with those failing is inflicted with pain especially by older women in the community.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Withholding colostrum from newborn
This involves depriving the newborn colostrum which is important for newborns in boosting their immunity. This is because, colostrum in some communities is considered dirty and bad omen.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Low levels of breast feeding
Some cultural and social beliefs and practices have an influence in breastfeeding. Despite the benefits of breastfeeding, in some</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
6
studocu
Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>communities, breastfeeding level is low due to sociocultural reasons.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="postpartum-nutritional-restriction">Postpartum nutritional restriction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#postpartum-nutritional-restriction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In many cultures, the belief in the avoidance of certain food intake (food taboos) protects the health of the mother leads to increased risk of deficiency of proteins, fats, vitamins A and calcium during lactation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vaginal-douching">Vaginal douching<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vaginal-douching" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Vaginal douching (VD) is the process of washing the vagina with water or other liquid solutions. VD can be widely seen in cultures that define the female body, menstruation and</p>
<p>sexual intercourse as dirty. Douching upsets the natural balance of bacteria in the vagina (called vaginal flora). These changes make the environment more favorable for the growth of bacteria that causes infections of the vagina.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="female-infanticide-and-son-preference">Female infanticide and son preference:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#female-infanticide-and-son-preference" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sex bias or son preference places the female child in a disadvantageous position from birth. In some communities, especially among the Asians, the practice of infanticide ensures that some female children have no life at all, violating the basic right to life. Selective abortion, foeticide and infanticide all occur because the female child is not valued by her culture, or because certain economic and legislative acts have ruled her life worthless</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="early-marriage-pregnancy-and-dowry-price">Early marriage, pregnancy and dowry price<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#early-marriage-pregnancy-and-dowry-price" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Early marriage is another serious problem which some girls, as opposed to boys, must face. The practice of giving away girls for marriage at the age of 11, 12 or 13, after which they must start producing children, is prevalent among certain ethnic groups in Asia and Africa. The principal reasons for this practice are the girls' virginity and the bride-price. Young girls are less likely to have had sexual contact and thus are believed to be virgins upon marriage; this condition raises the family status as well as the dowry to be paid by the husband. In some cases, virginity is verified by female relatives before the marriage</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dry-sex-practices-removal-of-vaginal-fluid-with-absorbent-materials">"Dry sex" practices (removal of vaginal fluid with absorbent materials)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dry-sex-practices-removal-of-vaginal-fluid-with-absorbent-materials" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Dry sex and virginity testing are useful and valuable traditional practices that seek to uphold cultural values in an increasingly westernized society. It could even be said that these two practices constitute appropriate responses to the HIV/AIDS pandemic in Africa. However, dry sex and virginity testing could also be seen as decidedly</p>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>harmful, in that they seek to maintain (and indeed entrench) the cultural and sexually based subordination of women in Africa.</p>
<p>Others include</p>
<ul>
<li>Breast and penis implants</li>
<li>Wife inheritance</li>
<li>Wife adoption</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="violence-against-women">Violence against Women<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#violence-against-women" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Violence against women is any act of gender-based violence that results in, or is likely to result in, physical, sexual, psychological harm or suffering to women, including threats of such acts, coercion or arbitrary deprivations of liberty, whether occurring in public or private.</li>
<li>Abuse of women and girls is best understood within gender framework because it stems in part from women's and girl's subordinate status in the society.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="violence-against-women-vam-encompasses-but-is-not-limited">Violence against women (VAM) encompasses, but is not limited;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#violence-against-women-vam-encompasses-but-is-not-limited" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Spousal battering</li>
<li>Sexual abuse of female children</li>
<li>Dowry-related violence</li>
<li>Rape including marital rape</li>
<li>Traditional practices harmful to women such as FGM.</li>
<li>Non-spousal violence</li>
<li>Sexual harassment and intimidation at work and in school</li>
<li>Trafficking in women</li>
<li>Forced prostitution</li>
<li>Violence perpetuated or condoned by the state, such as rape in war</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dealing-with-harmful-practices">Dealing with Harmful Practices<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dealing-with-harmful-practices" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Develop and support implementation of appropriate laws and policies.</li>
<li>Support community-level transformation of social norms and practices.</li>
<li>Empower women and girls to express and exercise their rights.</li>
<li>Increase access to quality prevention, protection and care services</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Birosoft Enterprises (<a href="mailto:birosoftenterprises@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">birosoftenterprises@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Increase global knowledge of the problem and political commitment to end child marriage and FGM</li>
<li>Increase government ownership over relevant programmes and efforts</li>
</ul>
